بتطليقة بانت ،بواحدة أمرك بيدك في ،تطليقة أو اختاري تطليقة فاختارت نفسها طلقت واحدة رجعيّة.
فصل
أي أو قال لها
بأن قالت اخترت نفسي
أمرك بيدك ينوي ثلاثاً، فقالت اخترت نفسي بواحدة . المرأة في جوابه
الرجعة
معنی
بمرة واحدة
بانت بواحدة [ أي بطلقة واحدة؛ لأن العامل فيه تخيير الزوج دون إيقاعها فإنها وإن أوقعت بالصريح، لكنه لا عبرة لإيقاعها، بل لتفويض الزوج. (ط، ع)] لأن العامل فيه تخيير الزوج لا إيقاعها، وذكر في الهداية: فهي واحدة يملك له، والصواب أنه لا يملك الرجعة؛ لأن المرأة إنما تتصرف حكما للتفويض، والتفويض غلط لا وهو بطلقة بائنة؛ لكونه من الكنايات فتملك الإبانة لا غير وقيل فيه روايتان إحداهما وقوع واحدة رجعية؛ لأن لفظها صريح ذكرها صدر الإسلام في الجامع الصغير، والأخرى وقوع البائنة، وهذا أصح ذكرها في الجامع الكبير
والمبسوط والزيادات، ألا ترى أن الزوج لو أمرها بالبائن أو الرجعي فعكست وقع ما نوى الزوج. (فتح، عيني) أمرك بيدك في تطليقة [ أي ولو قال لامرأته أمرك إلخ. (ط)] الأمر ههنا بمعنى الحال واليد بمعنى التصرف، وقيد بقوله: "في" تطليقة؛ لأنه لو قال: أمرك بيدك لو لم تصل نفقتي إليك فطلقي نفسك متى شئت" فلم تصل فطلقت كان بائناً؛ لأن لفظة الطلاق لم تكن في نفس الأمر. (فتح) طلقت واحدة رجعية: لأنه جعل الاختيار إليها ولكنه بتطليقة وهي معقبة للرجعة رمز الحقائق: ٢٤٨/١] فإن قيل: إن قوله: "أمرك بيدك" وقوله: أنه "اختاري" يفيد البينونة فلا يجوز صرفها عنه إلى غيرها، قلنا: لما قرن بالصريح علم رجعي كما لو قرن الصريح بالبائن بأن قال: أنت طالق بائن فإنه تبين به؛ لأنه أراد به البائن فكذا هذا. واعلم أن الطلاق الصريح لا يصير بائنا
بمجرد النية كما أن البائن لا يصير رجعيا بمجرد النية. (مستخلص، فتح) فصل: أي في بيان حكم الأمر باليد رمز الحقائق ٢٤٨/١٢] أمرك بيدك : أي لو قال رجل لامرأته: أمرك بيدك أو في كفك أو يمينك أو شمالك أو فمك أو لسانك. (ط) ينوي ثلاثاً : [ أي حال كونه ناويا بذلك ثلاثاً. (ع)] قيد بنية الثلاث؛ لأنه لو نوى واحدة أو ثنتين وكانت حرة أو لم ينو شيئاً وقعت واحدة، وقوله: "فقالت: اخترت نفسي" ذكر النفس خرج مخرج الشرط حتى لو لم تذكرها لا يقع كما لا يقع في جواب التخيير إلا بذكر النفس، ويقوم مقام ذكر النفس اخترت أمري أو قبلت نفسي، وكذا لو قالت في جواب الأمر باليد أنت علي حرام أو أنت مني بائن أو أنا منك بائن؛ لأن هذه الألفاظ تفيد الطلاق، وقوله: "وقعن"؛ لأن الاختيار يصلح لجواب الأمر باليد؛ لكونه تمليكاً كالتخيير، والواحدة صفة الاختيارة فصارت كأنها قالت اخترت نفسي بعمرة واحدة وبه يقع الثلاث، والحاصل: إن جعل الأمر بيدها كالتخيير في المسائل كلها إلا في احتمال الثلاثة، فإنه لا يصح نية في التخيير كما مر. (فتح، عيني)

كتاب الطلاق
حكم الأمر باليد
وقعن، وفي طلقت نفسي بواحدة أو اخترتُ نفسي بتطليقةٍ بانت بواحدة، ولا يدخل الليل في أمرُك بيدك اليوم وبعد غد، وإن ردّت الأمر في يومها بطل أمر ذلك اليوم،
تبين
أي المرأة المخيرة في المسألة المذكورة
وقعن: أي الثلاث؛ لأنه نوى محتمل كلامه (ع) وفي طلقت أي في قولها في جواب الزوج لما قال لها: أمرك بيدك. (ع) بواحدة: صفة لمصدر محذوف أي طلقت نفسي بتطليقة واحدة(ع) بانت بواحدة: [لأن الاعتبار بتفويض الزوج لا إيقاعها. (ع)] أي في المسألتين، أما الأولى : يعني لو قال الزوج لها: أمرك بيدك ونوى به ثلاثاً فقالت في جوابه: طلقت نفسي بواحدة فتبين بواحدة؛ لأن الواحدة صفة لمصدر محذوف تقديره طلقت نفسي بطلقة واحدة، وفي الثانية: أي لو قال لها: أمرك بيدك ونوى به ثلاثاً فقالت في جوابه: اخترت نفسي بتطليقة أيضاً بواحدة؛ لأن في جوابها تصريحا بالتطليقة وهي لا تكون إلا واحدة وإنما تكون بائنة؛ لأن المعتبر تفويض الزوج لا إيقاعها فتكون الصفة المذكورة في التفويض مذكورة في الجواب ضرورة الموافقة. وإنما صحت نية الثلاث في قوله: "أمرك بيدك"؛ لأن الأمر باليد تمليك فيملك تمليك ما يملكه قياسا واستحساناً، بخلاف التخيير؛ لأن وقوع الطلاق به على خلاف القياس لإجماع الصحابة فكان ضروريا، وذكر النفس في قولها: طلقت نفسي" في جواب الأمر باليد شرط حتى لو قال لها : أمرك بيدك فقالت: طلقت ولم تقل: نفسي لم يقع شيء. (مستخلص، فتح) ولا يدخل الليل لأن كل واحد من اليومين ذكر مفرداً، واليوم المفرد لا يتناول الليل، بخلاف الأيام؛ لأنها ينتظم ما بإزائها من الليالي مستخلص) وبعد غد فلا يكون لها الخيار بالليل حتى لو اختارت نفسها في الليل لا يقع الطلاق. (مص)
من غير
بطل أمر ذلك اليوم لأنه صرح بذكر وقتين اليوم وبعد غد أن بينهما وقت وهو الغد لم يتناول الأمر فعلم أنه ليس المراد بذكر الوقت الثاني امتداد الأمر الأول فاقتضى ضرورة إيجاب أمر آخر، فلما كانا أمرين ثبت لها الخيار في كل من الوقتين فإن ردت في اليوم لا يرتد بعد الغد، وقال زفر يبطل خيارها بعد غد أيضاً؛ لأنهما أمر واحد؛ لأنه عطف أحد الوقتين على الآخر تكرار لفظ الأمر، فيكون أمراً واحداً كما في الصورة الآتية أي اليوم وغداً، وكقوله: أنت طالق اليوم وبعد غد، قلنا: الأمر باليد يحتمل التوقيت لا حاجة إلى إدخال ما لم يدخل في اللفظ مقصوداً ولا تبعاً، فكانا أمرين ضرورة الانفصال، بخلاف الطلاق؛ لأنه لا يحتمل التوقيت فجاز أن يوصف في اليوم وبعد غد بطلاق واحد، فلا حاجة إلى إيقاع طلاق آخر ؛ لبقاء الأول إلى الوقت الثاني. وبخلاف قوله: "اليوم وغداً" على ما يأتي من الفرق أن الأمر باليد يحتمل التوقيت، فيتوقف الأمر بالأول ويجعل الثاني أمراً ابتداء، وعن أبي يوسف في الأمالي: " أنه إذا قال لامرأته : أمرك بيدك اليوم، وأمرك بيدك غداً إنهما أمران حتى إذا اختارت زوجها اليوم، ثم جاء الغد صار الأمر بيدها، وهو صحيح؛ لاستقلال كل واحد من الكلامين، فلا حاجة إلى الارتباط بما قبله، وينبغي أن يكون هذا بلا خلاف بينهم، ويتفرع عليه عدم جواز اختيارها نفسها ليلاً. (مستخلص، فتح)
Book of Divorce. Ruling of the command by hand: With one divorce, she becomes separated by one [divorce]. 'Your command is in your hand' in one divorce, or 'Choose' one divorce, and she chose herself, she is divorced by one revocable divorce. Section: Or he said to her: 'Your command is in your hand' intending three, and she said 'I have chosen myself with one.' The woman in her answer [produces] the meaning of revocable? With one time? She becomes separated by one [divorce] because the effective factor is the husband's delegation, not her execution; even if she executed explicitly, but no consideration is given to her execution, only to the husband's delegation. And it is mentioned in al-Hidayah: it is one [divorce] which he possesses, but the correct view is that he does not possess the right of return because the woman acts only as a result of the delegation, and the delegation is a mistake? It is an irrevocable divorce because it is from the kinayah, so she owns only the power of separation. And it is said there are two narrations: one is the occurrence of one revocable divorce because her wording is explicit, mentioned by Sadr al-Islam in al-Jami' al-Saghir, and the other is the occurrence of the irrevocable divorce, and this is more correct, mentioned in al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Mabsut, and al-Ziyadat. Do you not see that if the husband ordered her with the irrevocable or the revocable and she reversed, what the husband intended occurs. (Fath, 'Ayni) 'Your command is in your hand' in one divorce: meaning even if he said to his wife 'your command' etc. The word 'command' here means 'state' and 'hand' means 'disposal'. And he restricted it by 'in' one divorce because if he said: 'Your command is in your hand; if you do not receive my maintenance, then divorce yourself whenever you wish' and she did not receive [maintenance] and she divorced, it would be irrevocable because the word 'divorce' was not in the actual [statement]. (Fath) She is divorced by one revocable divorce because he gave her the choice but with one divorce which is followed by the right of return. [Ramooz al-Haqa'iq: 1/248] If it is said that his statement 'Your command is in your hand' and his statement 'Choose' indicate irrevocability, so it is not permissible to divert it to other than that, we say: Since it is associated with the explicit [wording], it is known to be revocable, just as if he associated the explicit with the irrevocable by saying 'You are divorced irrevocably', then she is separated by it because he intended the irrevocable. So likewise this. And know that explicit divorce does not become irrevocable by mere intention, just as the irrevocable does not become revocable by mere intention. (Mustakhlas, Fath) Section: explaining the ruling of the command by hand. [Ramooz al-Haqa'iq: 1/12] 'Your command is in your hand': meaning if a man said to his wife: 'Your command is in your hand' or 'in your palm' or 'your right hand' or 'your left hand' or 'your mouth' or 'your tongue'. (T) Intending three: meaning while intending thereby three. ('Ayni) He restricted it by intention of three because if he intended one or two and she was free, or he did not intend anything, one occurs. And his statement: 'she said: I have chosen myself' - mentioning 'self' is a condition such that if she does not mention it, it does not occur, just as it does not occur in the response of choice except with mentioning 'self', and 'I have chosen my affair' or 'I have accepted myself' stand in place of mentioning 'self'. Likewise if she says in response to the command by hand: 'You are forbidden to me' or 'You are irrevocable from me' or 'I am irrevocable from you', because these wordings indicate divorce. And his statement: 'they occur' because choice is suitable as a response to the command by hand since it is a form of delegation (tamlik) like choice (takhyeer), and 'one' is a description of the choice, so it is as if she said 'I have chosen myself with one divorce' and thereby the three occur. The conclusion: the command by hand is treated like choice (takhyeer) in all matters except regarding the possibility of three, for intention is not valid in choice (takhyeer) as has passed. (Fath, 'Ayni). They occur, and in 'I divorced myself with one' or 'I chose myself with one divorce' she is separated by one. And the night does not enter [the period] in 'your command is in your hand today and the day after tomorrow.' And if she rejects the command on her day, the command of that day becomes null. She becomes separated. Meaning the woman who is given choice in the mentioned matter. 'They occur': meaning the three because he intended what his speech can bear. ('Ayni) And in 'I divorced' meaning in her statement in response to the husband when he said to her: 'Your command is in your hand.' ('Ayni) 'With one': description of an omitted verbal noun, i.e., 'I divorced myself with one divorce.' ('Ayni) 'She is separated by one' because the consideration is given to the husband's delegation, not her execution. ('Ayni) That is in both matters. As for the first: meaning if the husband said to her: 'Your command is in your hand' and intended by it three, and she said in response: 'I divorced myself with one', she is separated by one because 'one' is a description of an omitted verbal noun, its implied form being 'I divorced myself with one divorce.' And in the second: meaning if he said to her: 'Your command is in your hand' and intended three, and she said in response: 'I chose myself with one divorce' also one, because in her response there is an explicit mention of the divorce, and it cannot be more than one, and it becomes irrevocable because the criterion is the husband's delegation, not her execution, so the description mentioned in the delegation is mentioned in the response necessarily for agreement. And the intention of three is valid in his statement 'your command is in your hand' because the command by hand is a delegation (tamlik), so he possesses the right to delegate what he possesses, by analogy and juristic preference (istihsan), unlike choice (takhyeer) because the occurrence of divorce by it is contrary to analogy due to the consensus of the Companions, so it was considered necessary. And the mention of 'self' in her statement 'I divorced myself' in response to the command by hand is a condition such that if he said to her: 'Your command is in your hand' and she said: 'I divorced' and did not say 'myself', nothing occurs. (Mustakhlas, Fath) And the night does not enter because each of the two days is mentioned individually, and a single day does not include the night, unlike days (plural) because they include what corresponds to them of nights. (Mustakhlas) And the day after tomorrow, so she has no choice during the night such that if she chooses herself at night, divorce does not occur. (MS) The command of that day becomes null because he explicitly mentioned two times: today and the day after tomorrow, and between them there is a time (tomorrow) that was not included in the command, so it is known that the intent of mentioning the second time is not extension of the first command, thus necessarily requiring another command. Since they are two commands, she has a choice in each of the two times; if she rejects on the day, it does not become null on the day after tomorrow. Zufar said that her choice after tomorrow also becomes null because they are a single command since the conjunction of one time to the other repeats the wording of the command, so it is one command as in the coming case, i.e., today and tomorrow, and like his statement: 'You are divorced today and the day after tomorrow.' We say: the command by hand admits of temporal fixation, so there is no need to include what was not included in the wording intentionally or incidentally, so they are two commands by necessity of separation, unlike divorce because it does not admit of temporal fixation, so it is possible for it to be described as one divorce in both today and the day after tomorrow, so there is no need to effect another divorce because the first continues until the second time. And unlike his statement 'today and tomorrow' as the difference will come that the command by hand admits of temporal fixation, so the first command stops and the second is made as an initial command. And from Abu Yusuf in al-Amali: that if he said to his wife: 'Your command is in your hand today, and your command is in your hand tomorrow' they are two commands such that if she chooses her husband today, then tomorrow comes, the command becomes in her hand, and this is correct because each of the two statements is independent, so there is no need for connection to what precedes. And it should be that there is no disagreement among them. And it branches from it that it is not permissible for her to choose herself at night. (Mustakhlas, Fath)
Source pages p. 426

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq, a foundational Hanafi text, discusses the ruling of 'amr bi yadik' (command by hand) in divorce. The author begins by stating a basic ruling: if a husband says to his wife 'Your command is in your hand' or 'Choose' with reference to one divorce, and she chooses herself, she is divorced by one revocable (raj'i) divorce. However, the commentary immediately clarifies that this is a summary; the detailed ruling is that it is actually an irrevocable (ba'in) divorce because such phrases are kinayah (allusive) and the wife only has the power to effect a ba'in divorce. There is a reported disagreement within the Hanafi school: some early texts state it is raj'i, but the majority (including al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Mabsut, al-Ziyadat) hold it is ba'in. The key principle is that the consideration is given to the husband's delegation, not the wife's execution. So even if the wife uses explicit wording, the nature of the divorce depends on the husband's delegation. The passage then addresses an objection: if 'amr bi yadik' indicates ba'in, how can it be interpreted as raj'i? The response is that when the husband couples it with an explicit term like 'with one divorce', it is understood as raj'i because the explicit term specifies revocability. This is analogous to saying 'You are divorced irrevocably'—the word 'ba'in' makes it irrevocable. However, intention alone cannot change the nature of explicit divorce (i.e., a clear 'You are divorced' remains raj'i unless accompanied by a qualifying word). The passage then moves to a separate section (fasl) on the ruling when the husband intends three divorces. If the husband says 'Your command is in your hand' intending three, and the wife responds 'I have chosen myself with one divorce', only one divorce occurs (ba'in). This is because the wife's response specifies one divorce, and the husband's intention of three is not effective beyond what the wife's words allow. However, if the wife says 'I have chosen myself' without specifying, and the husband intended three, three divorces occur. This is because 'amr bi yadik' is a delegation (tamlik), which can bear the intention of three, unlike takhyeer (choice), which is a concession and cannot. The passage also discusses the condition that the wife must mention 'self' (nafs) in her response; otherwise, no divorce occurs. It then addresses temporal issues: if the husband says 'Your command is in your hand today and the day after tomorrow', the night between them is not included, so choosing at night does not count. If the wife rejects the command on the day (e.g., by exercising her choice to stay married), the command for that day becomes null. There is a dispute with Zufar who considers the two times as one continuous command, but the Hanafi position, supported by Abu Yusuf, is that they are separate commands because 'amr bi yadik' admits of temporal specification. The practical result is that the wife has a separate choice period for each day, and night is not included.

Key Terms
تمليك (tamlik): Delegation of the power to divorce; the basis for 'amr bi yadik'.
تخيير (takhyeer): Giving the wife the choice to divorce or stay; a special concession.
نية (niyya): Intention of the husband regarding the number of divorces.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A husband says 'Your command is in your hand' intending three divorces. The wife responds 'I choose myself with one divorce.' How many divorces occur?
A) Three
B) One
C) None
D) Two

Key Takeaway
In 'amr bi yadik' (tamlik), the husband's intention of three takes effect if the wife does not limit her response; in takhyeer, intention of three is not valid.

Talaq — Divorce

10 min
Temporal Specification in 'Amr bi Yadik: Today and the Day After Tomorrow
Explaining the Hanafi position on temporal specification in 'amr bi yadik and the dispute with Zufar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule that 'amr bi yadik can be time-bound and explain the dispute with Zufar regarding separate vs continuous commands.

Core Idea
Each specified time in 'amr bi yadik creates a separate delegation; the night is not included.

This lesson addresses a temporal scenario: the husband says 'Your command is in your hand today and the day after tomorrow.' The Hanafi position, supported by Abu Yusuf, holds that these are two separate commands, so if the wife rejects on the first day, she still has a choice on the second. Zufar disagrees, arguing it is one continuous command. We will analyze the proof and practical outcome.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The husband delegates for two separate days: today and the day after tomorrow. There is a gap (tomorrow) not included.
The husband explicitly mentions two distinct times with a conjunction 'and'.
2
Apply the nature of 'amr bi yadik
'Amr bi yadik' admits temporal specification (tawqeet). It can be limited to a specific time period.
This is different from talaq (divorce) which does not admit temporal specification.
3
Analyze the two commands
Because each day is mentioned individually and there is a gap, they are two separate commands. The wife has a choice period in each day independently.
Rejection on one day does not affect the other.
4
Understand Zufar's objection
Zufar argues it is one command because the times are connected with 'and', similar to saying 'You are divorced today and the day after tomorrow' (which is one divorce covering both days).
He analogizes to explicit divorce wording.
5
Distinguish and conclude
Divorce does not admit temporal specification, so one divorce can be attached to two times. But 'amr bi yadik' does admit specification, so each time is a separate delegation. Also, the gap (tomorrow) not included shows they are separate.
Abu Yusuf's statement from al-Amali supports the two-command view.

بمرة واحدة
بانت بواحدة [ أي بطلقة واحدة؛ لأن العامل فيه تخيير الزوج دون إيقاعها فإنها وإن أوقعت بالصريح، لكنه لا عبرة لإيقاعها، بل لتفويض الزوج. (ط، ع)] لأن العامل فيه تخيير الزوج لا إيقاعها، وذكر في الهداية: فهي واحدة يملك له، والصواب أنه لا يملك الرجعة؛ لأن المرأة إنما تتصرف حكما للتفويض، والتفويض غلط لا وهو بطلقة بائنة؛ لكونه من الكنايات فتملك الإبانة لا غير وقيل فيه روايتان إحداهما وقوع واحدة رجعية؛ لأن لفظها صريح ذكرها صدر الإسلام في الجامع الصغير، والأخرى وقوع البائنة، وهذا أصح ذكرها في الجامع الكبير
والمبسوط والزيادات، ألا ترى أن الزوج لو أمرها بالبائن أو الرجعي فعكست وقع ما نوى الزوج. (فتح، عيني) أمرك بيدك في تطليقة [ أي ولو قال لامرأته أمرك إلخ. (ط)] الأمر ههنا بمعنى الحال واليد بمعنى التصرف، وقيد بقوله: "في" تطليقة؛ لأنه لو قال: أمرك بيدك لو لم تصل نفقتي إليك فطلقي نفسك متى شئت" فلم تصل فطلقت كان بائناً؛ لأن لفظة الطلاق لم تكن في نفس الأمر. (فتح) طلقت واحدة رجعية: لأنه جعل الاختيار إليها ولكنه بتطليقة وهي معقبة للرجعة رمز الحقائق: ٢٤٨/١] فإن قيل: إن قوله: "أمرك بيدك" وقوله: أنه "اختاري" يفيد البينونة فلا يجوز صرفها عنه إلى غيرها، قلنا: لما قرن بالصريح علم رجعي كما لو قرن الصريح بالبائن بأن قال: أنت طالق بائن فإنه تبين به؛ لأنه أراد به البائن فكذا هذا. واعلم أن الطلاق الصريح لا يصير بائنا
بمجرد النية كما أن البائن لا يصير رجعيا بمجرد النية. (مستخلص، فتح) فصل: أي في بيان حكم الأمر باليد رمز الحقائق ٢٤٨/١٢] أمرك بيدك : أي لو قال رجل لامرأته: أمرك بيدك أو في كفك أو يمينك أو شمالك أو فمك أو لسانك. (ط) ينوي ثلاثاً : [ أي حال كونه ناويا بذلك ثلاثاً. (ع)] قيد بنية الثلاث؛ لأنه لو نوى واحدة أو ثنتين وكانت حرة أو لم ينو شيئاً وقعت واحدة، وقوله: "فقالت: اخترت نفسي" ذكر النفس خرج مخرج الشرط حتى لو لم تذكرها لا يقع كما لا يقع في جواب التخيير إلا بذكر النفس، ويقوم مقام ذكر النفس اخترت أمري أو قبلت نفسي، وكذا لو قالت في جواب الأمر باليد أنت علي حرام أو أنت مني بائن أو أنا منك بائن؛ لأن هذه الألفاظ تفيد الطلاق، وقوله: "وقعن"؛ لأن الاختيار يصلح لجواب الأمر باليد؛ لكونه تمليكاً كالتخيير، والواحدة صفة الاختيارة فصارت كأنها قالت اخترت نفسي بعمرة واحدة وبه يقع الثلاث، والحاصل: إن جعل الأمر بيدها كالتخيير في المسائل كلها إلا في احتمال الثلاثة، فإنه لا يصح نية في التخيير كما مر. (فتح، عيني)

كتاب الطلاق
حكم الأمر باليد
وقعن، وفي طلقت نفسي بواحدة أو اخترتُ نفسي بتطليقةٍ بانت بواحدة، ولا يدخل الليل في أمرُك بيدك اليوم وبعد غد، وإن ردّت الأمر في يومها بطل أمر ذلك اليوم،
تبين
أي المرأة المخيرة في المسألة المذكورة
وقعن: أي الثلاث؛ لأنه نوى محتمل كلامه (ع) وفي طلقت أي في قولها في جواب الزوج لما قال لها: أمرك بيدك. (ع) بواحدة: صفة لمصدر محذوف أي طلقت نفسي بتطليقة واحدة(ع) بانت بواحدة: [لأن الاعتبار بتفويض الزوج لا إيقاعها. (ع)] أي في المسألتين، أما الأولى : يعني لو قال الزوج لها: أمرك بيدك ونوى به ثلاثاً فقالت في جوابه: طلقت نفسي بواحدة فتبين بواحدة؛ لأن الواحدة صفة لمصدر محذوف تقديره طلقت نفسي بطلقة واحدة، وفي الثانية: أي لو قال لها: أمرك بيدك ونوى به ثلاثاً فقالت في جوابه: اخترت نفسي بتطليقة أيضاً بواحدة؛ لأن في جوابها تصريحا بالتطليقة وهي لا تكون إلا واحدة وإنما تكون بائنة؛ لأن المعتبر تفويض الزوج لا إيقاعها فتكون الصفة المذكورة في التفويض مذكورة في الجواب ضرورة الموافقة. وإنما صحت نية الثلاث في قوله: "أمرك بيدك"؛ لأن الأمر باليد تمليك فيملك تمليك ما يملكه قياسا واستحساناً، بخلاف التخيير؛ لأن وقوع الطلاق به على خلاف القياس لإجماع الصحابة فكان ضروريا، وذكر النفس في قولها: طلقت نفسي" في جواب الأمر باليد شرط حتى لو قال لها : أمرك بيدك فقالت: طلقت ولم تقل: نفسي لم يقع شيء. (مستخلص، فتح) ولا يدخل الليل لأن كل واحد من اليومين ذكر مفرداً، واليوم المفرد لا يتناول الليل، بخلاف الأيام؛ لأنها ينتظم ما بإزائها من الليالي مستخلص) وبعد غد فلا يكون لها الخيار بالليل حتى لو اختارت نفسها في الليل لا يقع الطلاق. (مص)
من غير
بطل أمر ذلك اليوم لأنه صرح بذكر وقتين اليوم وبعد غد أن بينهما وقت وهو الغد لم يتناول الأمر فعلم أنه ليس المراد بذكر الوقت الثاني امتداد الأمر الأول فاقتضى ضرورة إيجاب أمر آخر، فلما كانا أمرين ثبت لها الخيار في كل من الوقتين فإن ردت في اليوم لا يرتد بعد الغد، وقال زفر يبطل خيارها بعد غد أيضاً؛ لأنهما أمر واحد؛ لأنه عطف أحد الوقتين على الآخر تكرار لفظ الأمر، فيكون أمراً واحداً كما في الصورة الآتية أي اليوم وغداً، وكقوله: أنت طالق اليوم وبعد غد، قلنا: الأمر باليد يحتمل التوقيت لا حاجة إلى إدخال ما لم يدخل في اللفظ مقصوداً ولا تبعاً، فكانا أمرين ضرورة الانفصال، بخلاف الطلاق؛ لأنه لا يحتمل التوقيت فجاز أن يوصف في اليوم وبعد غد بطلاق واحد، فلا حاجة إلى إيقاع طلاق آخر ؛ لبقاء الأول إلى الوقت الثاني. وبخلاف قوله: "اليوم وغداً" على ما يأتي من الفرق أن الأمر باليد يحتمل التوقيت، فيتوقف الأمر بالأول ويجعل الثاني أمراً ابتداء، وعن أبي يوسف في الأمالي: " أنه إذا قال لامرأته : أمرك بيدك اليوم، وأمرك بيدك غداً إنهما أمران حتى إذا اختارت زوجها اليوم، ثم جاء الغد صار الأمر بيدها، وهو صحيح؛ لاستقلال كل واحد من الكلامين، فلا حاجة إلى الارتباط بما قبله، وينبغي أن يكون هذا بلا خلاف بينهم، ويتفرع عليه عدم جواز اختيارها نفسها ليلاً. (مستخلص، فتح)
Book of Divorce. Ruling of the command by hand: With one divorce, she becomes separated by one [divorce]. 'Your command is in your hand' in one divorce, or 'Choose' one divorce, and she chose herself, she is divorced by one revocable divorce. Section: Or he said to her: 'Your command is in your hand' intending three, and she said 'I have chosen myself with one.' The woman in her answer [produces] the meaning of revocable? With one time? She becomes separated by one [divorce] because the effective factor is the husband's delegation, not her execution; even if she executed explicitly, but no consideration is given to her execution, only to the husband's delegation. And it is mentioned in al-Hidayah: it is one [divorce] which he possesses, but the correct view is that he does not possess the right of return because the woman acts only as a result of the delegation, and the delegation is a mistake? It is an irrevocable divorce because it is from the kinayah, so she owns only the power of separation. And it is said there are two narrations: one is the occurrence of one revocable divorce because her wording is explicit, mentioned by Sadr al-Islam in al-Jami' al-Saghir, and the other is the occurrence of the irrevocable divorce, and this is more correct, mentioned in al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Mabsut, and al-Ziyadat. Do you not see that if the husband ordered her with the irrevocable or the revocable and she reversed, what the husband intended occurs. (Fath, 'Ayni) 'Your command is in your hand' in one divorce: meaning even if he said to his wife 'your command' etc. The word 'command' here means 'state' and 'hand' means 'disposal'. And he restricted it by 'in' one divorce because if he said: 'Your command is in your hand; if you do not receive my maintenance, then divorce yourself whenever you wish' and she did not receive [maintenance] and she divorced, it would be irrevocable because the word 'divorce' was not in the actual [statement]. (Fath) She is divorced by one revocable divorce because he gave her the choice but with one divorce which is followed by the right of return. [Ramooz al-Haqa'iq: 1/248] If it is said that his statement 'Your command is in your hand' and his statement 'Choose' indicate irrevocability, so it is not permissible to divert it to other than that, we say: Since it is associated with the explicit [wording], it is known to be revocable, just as if he associated the explicit with the irrevocable by saying 'You are divorced irrevocably', then she is separated by it because he intended the irrevocable. So likewise this. And know that explicit divorce does not become irrevocable by mere intention, just as the irrevocable does not become revocable by mere intention. (Mustakhlas, Fath) Section: explaining the ruling of the command by hand. [Ramooz al-Haqa'iq: 1/12] 'Your command is in your hand': meaning if a man said to his wife: 'Your command is in your hand' or 'in your palm' or 'your right hand' or 'your left hand' or 'your mouth' or 'your tongue'. (T) Intending three: meaning while intending thereby three. ('Ayni) He restricted it by intention of three because if he intended one or two and she was free, or he did not intend anything, one occurs. And his statement: 'she said: I have chosen myself' - mentioning 'self' is a condition such that if she does not mention it, it does not occur, just as it does not occur in the response of choice except with mentioning 'self', and 'I have chosen my affair' or 'I have accepted myself' stand in place of mentioning 'self'. Likewise if she says in response to the command by hand: 'You are forbidden to me' or 'You are irrevocable from me' or 'I am irrevocable from you', because these wordings indicate divorce. And his statement: 'they occur' because choice is suitable as a response to the command by hand since it is a form of delegation (tamlik) like choice (takhyeer), and 'one' is a description of the choice, so it is as if she said 'I have chosen myself with one divorce' and thereby the three occur. The conclusion: the command by hand is treated like choice (takhyeer) in all matters except regarding the possibility of three, for intention is not valid in choice (takhyeer) as has passed. (Fath, 'Ayni). They occur, and in 'I divorced myself with one' or 'I chose myself with one divorce' she is separated by one. And the night does not enter [the period] in 'your command is in your hand today and the day after tomorrow.' And if she rejects the command on her day, the command of that day becomes null. She becomes separated. Meaning the woman who is given choice in the mentioned matter. 'They occur': meaning the three because he intended what his speech can bear. ('Ayni) And in 'I divorced' meaning in her statement in response to the husband when he said to her: 'Your command is in your hand.' ('Ayni) 'With one': description of an omitted verbal noun, i.e., 'I divorced myself with one divorce.' ('Ayni) 'She is separated by one' because the consideration is given to the husband's delegation, not her execution. ('Ayni) That is in both matters. As for the first: meaning if the husband said to her: 'Your command is in your hand' and intended by it three, and she said in response: 'I divorced myself with one', she is separated by one because 'one' is a description of an omitted verbal noun, its implied form being 'I divorced myself with one divorce.' And in the second: meaning if he said to her: 'Your command is in your hand' and intended three, and she said in response: 'I chose myself with one divorce' also one, because in her response there is an explicit mention of the divorce, and it cannot be more than one, and it becomes irrevocable because the criterion is the husband's delegation, not her execution, so the description mentioned in the delegation is mentioned in the response necessarily for agreement. And the intention of three is valid in his statement 'your command is in your hand' because the command by hand is a delegation (tamlik), so he possesses the right to delegate what he possesses, by analogy and juristic preference (istihsan), unlike choice (takhyeer) because the occurrence of divorce by it is contrary to analogy due to the consensus of the Companions, so it was considered necessary. And the mention of 'self' in her statement 'I divorced myself' in response to the command by hand is a condition such that if he said to her: 'Your command is in your hand' and she said: 'I divorced' and did not say 'myself', nothing occurs. (Mustakhlas, Fath) And the night does not enter because each of the two days is mentioned individually, and a single day does not include the night, unlike days (plural) because they include what corresponds to them of nights. (Mustakhlas) And the day after tomorrow, so she has no choice during the night such that if she chooses herself at night, divorce does not occur. (MS) The command of that day becomes null because he explicitly mentioned two times: today and the day after tomorrow, and between them there is a time (tomorrow) that was not included in the command, so it is known that the intent of mentioning the second time is not extension of the first command, thus necessarily requiring another command. Since they are two commands, she has a choice in each of the two times; if she rejects on the day, it does not become null on the day after tomorrow. Zufar said that her choice after tomorrow also becomes null because they are a single command since the conjunction of one time to the other repeats the wording of the command, so it is one command as in the coming case, i.e., today and tomorrow, and like his statement: 'You are divorced today and the day after tomorrow.' We say: the command by hand admits of temporal fixation, so there is no need to include what was not included in the wording intentionally or incidentally, so they are two commands by necessity of separation, unlike divorce because it does not admit of temporal fixation, so it is possible for it to be described as one divorce in both today and the day after tomorrow, so there is no need to effect another divorce because the first continues until the second time. And unlike his statement 'today and tomorrow' as the difference will come that the command by hand admits of temporal fixation, so the first command stops and the second is made as an initial command. And from Abu Yusuf in al-Amali: that if he said to his wife: 'Your command is in your hand today, and your command is in your hand tomorrow' they are two commands such that if she chooses her husband today, then tomorrow comes, the command becomes in her hand, and this is correct because each of the two statements is independent, so there is no need for connection to what precedes. And it should be that there is no disagreement among them. And it branches from it that it is not permissible for her to choose herself at night. (Mustakhlas, Fath)
Source pages p. 426

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq, a foundational Hanafi text, discusses the ruling of 'amr bi yadik' (command by hand) in divorce. The author begins by stating a basic ruling: if a husband says to his wife 'Your command is in your hand' or 'Choose' with reference to one divorce, and she chooses herself, she is divorced by one revocable (raj'i) divorce. However, the commentary immediately clarifies that this is a summary; the detailed ruling is that it is actually an irrevocable (ba'in) divorce because such phrases are kinayah (allusive) and the wife only has the power to effect a ba'in divorce. There is a reported disagreement within the Hanafi school: some early texts state it is raj'i, but the majority (including al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Mabsut, al-Ziyadat) hold it is ba'in. The key principle is that the consideration is given to the husband's delegation, not the wife's execution. So even if the wife uses explicit wording, the nature of the divorce depends on the husband's delegation. The passage then addresses an objection: if 'amr bi yadik' indicates ba'in, how can it be interpreted as raj'i? The response is that when the husband couples it with an explicit term like 'with one divorce', it is understood as raj'i because the explicit term specifies revocability. This is analogous to saying 'You are divorced irrevocably'—the word 'ba'in' makes it irrevocable. However, intention alone cannot change the nature of explicit divorce (i.e., a clear 'You are divorced' remains raj'i unless accompanied by a qualifying word). The passage then moves to a separate section (fasl) on the ruling when the husband intends three divorces. If the husband says 'Your command is in your hand' intending three, and the wife responds 'I have chosen myself with one divorce', only one divorce occurs (ba'in). This is because the wife's response specifies one divorce, and the husband's intention of three is not effective beyond what the wife's words allow. However, if the wife says 'I have chosen myself' without specifying, and the husband intended three, three divorces occur. This is because 'amr bi yadik' is a delegation (tamlik), which can bear the intention of three, unlike takhyeer (choice), which is a concession and cannot. The passage also discusses the condition that the wife must mention 'self' (nafs) in her response; otherwise, no divorce occurs. It then addresses temporal issues: if the husband says 'Your command is in your hand today and the day after tomorrow', the night between them is not included, so choosing at night does not count. If the wife rejects the command on the day (e.g., by exercising her choice to stay married), the command for that day becomes null. There is a dispute with Zufar who considers the two times as one continuous command, but the Hanafi position, supported by Abu Yusuf, is that they are separate commands because 'amr bi yadik' admits of temporal specification. The practical result is that the wife has a separate choice period for each day, and night is not included.

Key Terms
توقيت (tawqeet): Temporal specification; limiting a legal act to a specific time.
رد الأمر (radd al-amr): Rejecting the command; if the wife does not divorce within the specified time, the command becomes null.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A husband says 'Your command is in your hand today and the day after tomorrow.' According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, if the wife does not divorce on the first day, what happens to her choice on the second day?
A) She loses it because it was one continuous command
B) She still has the choice on the second day
C) She only retains the choice if she did not reject the first command
D) The night between invalidates both commands

Key Takeaway
When 'amr bi yadik' is specified for two separate days, they are two independent delegations; the night is not included, and rejection on one day does not affect the other.

Talaq — Divorce
beginner
8 min
The Delegation of Divorce and the Husband's Intention
Ruling on husband's intention and the condition of mentioning 'nafsi'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how the husband's intention determines the effect of the wife's pronouncement in amr bil-yad and identify the condition of mentioning 'nafsi'.

Core Idea
In amr bil-yad, the husband's delegation controls; the wife's pronouncement merely executes it.

When a husband delegates the power of divorce to his wife (amr bil-yad), his intention regarding the number of divorces is decisive, not the wife's actual wording. If he intends three but she says 'one', only one irrevocable divorce occurs. This lesson also clarifies the essential condition that she must say 'nafsi' (myself) for the divorce to take effect.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its basis
State that amr bil-yad is a valid form of delegation (tamlik). The husband's intention is considered because he owns the right to divorce and can grant what he owns, by qiyas and istihsan.
The evidence includes Ijma al-Sahabah for the validity of delegation.
2
Trace the effect of intention
If the husband intends three divorces but the wife says 'I divorce myself with one', only one ba'in divorce occurs. The adjective 'one' in her response refers to the omitted source noun, and the decisive factor is the husband's delegation.
The wife's response must match the delegation in number; here it is compatible because she mentions one, which does not exceed his intended three.
3
Apply the condition of 'nafsi'
The wife must say 'nafsi' in her reply (e.g., 'I divorced myself'). If she says only 'I divorced' without 'myself', no divorce occurs. This is a necessary condition.
This underscores that the wife is the object of the divorce, and the pronoun must refer to herself.
4
Distinguish from takhyir
Amr bil-yad is tamlik (granting ownership) and thus valid by qiyas and istihsan. Takhyir (giving choice without full delegation) is restricted and not treated the same way.
Takhyir is based on Ijma but is a constrained exception; it does not allow the husband to stipulate the number.

(ع) بواحدة: صفة لمصدر محذوف أي طلقت نفسي بتطليقة واحدة(ع) بانت بواحدة: [لأن الاعتبار بتفويض الزوج لا إيقاعها. (ع)] أي في المسألتين، أما الأولى : يعني لو قال الزوج لها: أمرك بيدك ونوى به ثلاثاً فقالت في جوابه: طلقت نفسي بواحدة فتبين بواحدة؛ لأن الواحدة صفة لمصدر محذوف تقديره طلقت نفسي بطلقة واحدة، وفي الثانية: أي لو قال لها: أمرك بيدك ونوى به ثلاثاً فقالت في جوابه: اخترت نفسي بتطليقة أيضاً بواحدة؛ لأن في جوابها تصريحا بالتطليقة وهي لا تكون إلا واحدة وإنما تكون بائنة؛ لأن المعتبر تفويض الزوج لا إيقاعها فتكون الصفة المذكورة في التفويض مذكورة في الجواب ضرورة الموافقة. وإنما صحت نية الثلاث في قوله: "أمرك بيدك"؛ لأن الأمر باليد تمليك فيملك تمليك ما يملكه قياسا واستحساناً، بخلاف التخيير؛ لأن وقوع الطلاق به على خلاف القياس لإجماع الصحابة فكان ضروريا، وذكر النفس في قولها: طلقت نفسي" في جواب الأمر باليد شرط حتى لو قال لها : أمرك بيدك فقالت: طلقت ولم تقل: نفسي لم يقع شيء. (مستخلص، فتح) ولا يدخل الليل لأن كل واحد من اليومين ذكر مفرداً، واليوم المفرد لا يتناول الليل، بخلاف الأيام؛ لأنها ينتظم ما بإزائها من الليالي مستخلص) وبعد غد فلا يكون لها الخيار بالليل حتى لو اختارت نفسها في الليل لا يقع الطلاق. (مص) من غير بطل أمر ذلك اليوم لأنه صرح بذكر وقتين اليوم وبعد غد أن بينهما وقت وهو الغد لم يتناول الأمر فعلم أنه ليس المراد بذكر الوقت الثاني امتداد الأمر الأول فاقتضى ضرورة إيجاب أمر آخر، فلما كانا أمرين ثبت لها الخيار في كل من الوقتين فإن ردت في اليوم لا يرتد بعد الغد، وقال زفر يبطل خيارها بعد غد أيضاً؛ لأنهما أمر واحد؛ لأنه عطف أحد الوقتين على الآخر تكرار لفظ الأمر، فيكون أمراً واحداً كما في الصورة الآتية أي اليوم وغداً، وكقوله: أنت طالق اليوم وبعد غد، قلنا: الأمر باليد يحتمل التوقيت لا حاجة إلى إدخال ما لم يدخل في اللفظ مقصوداً ولا تبعاً، فكانا أمرين ضرورة الانفصال، بخلاف الطلاق؛ لأنه لا يحتمل التوقيت فجاز أن يوصف في اليوم وبعد غد بطلاق واحد، فلا حاجة إلى إيقاع طلاق آخر ؛ لبقاء الأول إلى الوقت الثاني. وبخلاف قوله: "اليوم وغداً" على ما يأتي من الفرق أن الأمر باليد يحتمل التوقيت، فيتوقف الأمر بالأول ويجعل الثاني أمراً ابتداء، وعن أبي يوسف في الأمالي: " أنه إذا قال لامرأته : أمرك بيدك اليوم، وأمرك بيدك غداً إنهما أمران حتى إذا اختارت زوجها اليوم، ثم جاء الغد صار الأمر بيدها، وهو صحيح؛ لاستقلال كل واحد من الكلامين، فلا حاجة إلى الارتباط بما قبله، وينبغي أن يكون هذا بلا خلاف بينهم، ويتفرع عليه عدم جواز اختيارها نفسها ليلاً. (مستخلص، فتح) وكان الأمر بيدها بعد غد، وفي أمرك بيدك اليوم وغداً يدخل، وإن ردّت في أي المخيرة الأمر يومها لم يبق الأمر في الغد، ولو مكثت بعد التفويض يوماً ولم تقم، أو جلست في هذه المسألة بيدها أي المرأة المطلق عنه أو اتكأت عن قعود أو عكست أو دعت أباها للمشورة. أي عن القيام بأن كانت متكتة فقعدت أي طلبت أو أكثر و برد أحدهما لا يرد غد: لأنهما أمران لانفصال وقتهما فثبت لها الخيار في كل واحد من الوقتين على حدة الآخر. (ع) وفي أمرك أي في قوله لامرأته : أمرك إلخ. (ط) يدخل [ أي الليل في ذلك ويكون وقت الاختيار ممتدا إلى غروب الشمس من الغد. (ط)] أي يدخل الليل في قوله لها : أمرك بيدك اليوم وغدا؛ لأنه لم يتخلل بين الوقتين وقت من جنسهما لم يتناوله للأمر، فكان أمراً واحداً فإن قلت اليوم ههنا ذكر مفرداً فوجب أن يتناول الليل كالمسألة الأولى؟ قلت الجمع بينهما بحرف الجمع وهو الواو كالجمع بلفظة الجمع، فصار كقوله: "أمرك بيدك يومين" ولا يمكن ذلك في المسألة الأولى إلى اليوم وبعد غد؛ لتخلل وقت من جنسهما وهو الغد لم يدخل تحت اللفظ، وههنا أمكن؛ لعدم التخلل حتى لو قال هناك أيضاً أمرك بيدك اليوم وغداً وبعد غد كان أمراً واحداً للاتصال. [رمز الحقائق: ٢٤٩/١] (فتح) 11 لم يبق الأمر في الغد: لأنه أمر واحد، فلا يبقى لها الخيار بعد الرد كما إذا قال لها: أمرك بيدك اليوم فردته في أول النهار لا يبقى لها الخيار في آخره، وعن أبي حنيفة أنها إذا ردت الأمر في اليوم لها أن تختار نفسها غدا؛ لأنها لا تملك رد الأمر كما لا تملك رد الإيقاع، والجامع عدم اشتراط القبول فيهما في المجلس فصار بمنزلة قيامها عن المجلس، واشتغالها بعمل آخر وجه الظاهر أن المدة كلها بمنزلة المجلس فيما لم يذكر الوقت فيه؛ لكونه أمراً واحداً، وهناك لم يثبت لها الخيار بعد الرد فكذا هنا؛ ولأن من له الخيار بين شيئين إذا اختار أحدهما لا يكون له خيار الآخر، ألا تری أنها لو اختارت نفسها اليوم ليس لها أن تختار زوجها غداً فكذا هذا، وعن محمد: لو قال لامرأته: "أمرك بيدك "اليوم كان لها الخيار إلى غروب الشمس، ولو قال: أمرك بيدك في اليوم" كان لها الخيار في المجلس، فإذا قامت بطل، وهو كقوله : أنت طالق غداً وفي غد تبيين الحقائق: ٩٣/٣] (فتح) ولم تقم ولم تأخذ في عمل آخر. (ط)] المراد بالقيام المنفي ما يدل على الإعراض لا خصوص القيام، وهذا إذا كان التفويض مطلقاً، وأما إذا كان مؤقتاً فلا يبطل بالقيام ونحوه، وإنما يبطل الخيار بمضي الوقت وإن لم تقم، وإنما قيد بقوله : " لم تقم"؛ لأنها إذا قامت أو أخذت في عمل آخر خرج الأمر يدها كما مر، وقوله: "للمشورة" قال في المصباح شاورته واستشرته والاسم المشورة وفيها لغتان سكون الشين وفتح الواو، وضم الشين وسكون الواو، نقل الحموي أن المشورة بوزن المعونة هي اللغة الفصيحة الصحيحة، وفيها لغة أخرى مشورة كقسورة. (فتح) للمشورة بفتح الميم وضم الشين وفتح الراء وهي المشاورة. (ع) من
Book of Divorce. Ruling of the command by hand: they fall [three?]. And in 'I divorced myself with one' or 'I chose myself with a divorce', she becomes irrevocably divorced by one. And the night does not enter in 'your command is in your hand today and the day after tomorrow'. And if she rejects the command on her day, the command of that day is nullified. As for the woman given choice in the mentioned issue: 'they fall' means three because he intended [that is, his speech permits it]. And in 'I divorced myself' means in her reply to the husband when he said 'your command is in your hand'. 'With one' is an adjective for an omitted accusative source noun, i.e., I divorced myself with one divorce. 'She becomes irrevocably divorced by one' because the consideration is the husband's delegation, not her execution. In the two issues: the first: if the husband said to her 'your command is in your hand' and intended three, and she said in reply 'I divorced myself with one', then she is irrevocably divorced by one because 'one' is an adjective for an omitted source noun. And the second: if he said to her 'your command is in your hand' and intended three, and she said in reply 'I chose myself with a divorce', also by one, because in her reply there is explicit mention of a divorce which cannot be except one, and it is only irrevocable because the consideration is the husband's delegation, not her execution, so the mentioned adjective in the delegation is necessary in the reply for agreement. The intention of three in his saying 'your command is in your hand' is valid because the command by hand is a granting of ownership, so he owns granting what he owns, by analogy and juristic preference, unlike choice because divorce occurs by it contrary to analogy due to the consensus of the Companions, so it is constrained. And the mention of 'myself' in her saying 'I divorced myself' in reply to the command by hand is a condition: if he said to her 'your command is in your hand' and she said 'I divorced' without saying 'myself', nothing occurs. The night does not enter because each of the two days is mentioned individually, and the individual day does not include the night, unlike days because they include the nights corresponding to them. And 'the day after tomorrow': so she has no choice at night, and if she chose herself at night, divorce does not occur. The command of that day is nullified because he explicitly mentioned two times—today and the day after tomorrow—and between them there is a time, which is tomorrow, not covered by the command, so it is known that the mention of the second time was not meant to extend the first command, thus necessarily entailing a separate command. Since they are two commands, she has a choice in each of the two times; if she rejects on the first day, she does not lose the option for the day after tomorrow. Zufar said: her choice for the day after tomorrow is also nullified because they are one command due to the conjunction of one time to the other and the repetition of the word 'command', so it is one command as in the subsequent case (i.e., today and tomorrow) and like his saying 'you are divorced today and the day after tomorrow'. We said: the command by hand is susceptible to temporal specification; there is no need to include what is not included in the wording intentionally or incidentally, so they are two commands by necessity of separation, unlike divorce because it is not susceptible to temporal specification, so it is permissible for it to be described in 'today and the day after tomorrow' as one divorce; there is no need to effect another divorce because the first remains until the second time. And unlike his saying 'today and tomorrow', as the difference will come: that the command by hand is susceptible to temporal specification, so the first command is suspended and the second is made an initial command. And from Abu Yusuf in al-Amali: that if he said to his wife 'your command is in your hand today, and your command is in your hand tomorrow', they are two commands, so if she chooses her husband today, then when tomorrow comes, the command is in her hand, and this is correct because each statement is independent, so there is no need for connection to what preceded. And it should be that this is without disagreement among them, and it follows from it that she is not allowed to choose herself at night. The command is in her hand after the day after tomorrow. And in 'your command is in your hand today and tomorrow', it enters. And if she rejects the command on her day, the command does not remain for tomorrow. And if she remains after the delegation for a day without standing, or sits—in this issue, 'in her hand' means the woman from whom the divorce is being sought—or leans from sitting, or reverses, or calls her father for consultation. The negation of standing refers to what indicates disinterest, not specifically standing. And this is when the delegation is absolute; if it is time-bound, it is not nullified by standing and the like; rather, the choice is nullified by the passing of time even if she does not stand. And it is restricted by 'she did not stand' because when she stands or engages in another act, the command leaves her hand as previously mentioned. And his saying 'for consultation'—in al-Misbah: shawartuhu and istashartu, and the noun is mashwarah, with two dialects: sukun of shin and fatha of waw, and damm of shin and sukun of waw. al-Hamawi transmitted that ma-shu-ra (like ma'oona) is the eloquent correct dialect, and another dialect is mashurah like qaswurah. For consultation: with fatha of mim, damm of shin, and fatha of ra, and it is the same as mashawarah.
Source pages p. 427

Commentary
This passage from Kanzuldaqaiq discusses the rulings on the husband delegating the power of divorce to the wife (amr bil-yad). The text first addresses the effect of the husband's intention when delegating. If the husband intends three divorces but the wife responds with 'I divorce myself with one' or 'I choose myself with a single divorce', only one irrevocable divorce (ba'in) occurs. This is because the decisive factor is the husband's delegation, not the wife's execution; her response must match the delegation. The husband's intention of three is validated by the principle that amr bil-yad is a form of tamlik (granting ownership), so he can grant what he owns, based on qiyas and istihsan. The mention of 'nafsi' (myself) is a condition—if she omits it, no divorce occurs. Next, the text rules on time specifications. When the husband says 'today and the day after tomorrow', the night period between them is not included, and she cannot choose at night. Each day is a separate command, so if she rejects on the first day, her option for the second remains. Zufar disagrees, considering them one command, but the Hanafi position is that they are separate because amr bil-yad can be temporally specified. Abu Yusuf's view from al-Amali supports this. When the husband says 'today and tomorrow' without 'after', the night is included, and it is a single command. Rejection on the first day nullifies the option for the next day. Lastly, the text discusses the effect of the wife's actions after delegation. If she remains seated without standing or engaging in another activity, her option continues. Standing or starting another task indicates disinterest and nullifies the option. This applies to absolute delegation; if time-bound, only the expiry of time nullifies it. Consulting her father for advice does not nullify the option.

Key Terms
الأمر باليد (al-amr bil-yad): The husband's delegation of the power to divorce to the wife, giving her the option to choose herself or her husband.
بائنة (ba'inah): An irrevocable divorce that ends the marriage immediately without the possibility of revocability.
التفويض (al-tafwid): In this context, the husband's delegation of the divorce decision to the wife.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a husband says to his wife 'Your command is in your hand' intending three divorces, and she replies 'I divorced myself' without saying 'myself' (nafsi), what is the ruling?
A) One irrevocable divorce occurs
B) Three divorces occur
C) No divorce occurs
D) One revocable divorce occurs

Key Takeaway
In amr bil-yad, the husband's intention controls the number of divorces, and the wife must say 'nafsi' for the pronouncement to be effective.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
10 min
Temporal Separation in Amr bil-Yad: Two Commands vs One
Intra-Hanafi dispute on temporal specification in amr bil-yad

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between two temporal formulas in amr bil-yad and state the Hanafi position and the dispute with Zufar.

Core Idea
'Today and after tomorrow' are two separate commands; 'today and tomorrow' is one continuous command.

The husband may delegate divorce with a time specification. The wording 'today and after tomorrow' creates two independent options because a day (tomorrow) intervenes. In contrast, 'today and tomorrow' is a single continuous period, including the night in between. Zufar differed, but the majority Hanafi position prevails.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two formulas
Note the two examples: (1) 'your command is in your hand today and the day after tomorrow' (بعد غد). (2) 'your command is in your hand today and tomorrow' (وغداً).
The difference is the word 'after' creating a gap.
2
Analyze the legal effect of each
In formula (1), each day is a separate command; rejection on the first does not affect the second. The night between is not included. In formula (2), it is a single command; rejection any time within the period nullifies the option entirely, and the night is included.
The key is whether there is an intervening time not covered by the command.
3
Examine Zufar's objection
Zufar argues that both formulas are one command because the word 'command' is repeated and the times are conjoined. He analogizes to divorce pronouncement (e.g., 'you are divorced today and after tomorrow') which is one divorce.
The Hanafi response: amr bil-yad can be temporally specified (yahtamil al-tawqit), unlike divorce itself.
4
Determine the Hanafi tarjih
The majority (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) holds that formula (1) is two commands. Zufar's view is not mufta bihi.
Abu Yusuf's narration in al-Amali confirms the two-command view for 'today and tomorrow' when the command is repeated.

(مص) من غير بطل أمر ذلك اليوم لأنه صرح بذكر وقتين اليوم وبعد غد أن بينهما وقت وهو الغد لم يتناول الأمر فعلم أنه ليس المراد بذكر الوقت الثاني امتداد الأمر الأول فاقتضى ضرورة إيجاب أمر آخر، فلما كانا أمرين ثبت لها الخيار في كل من الوقتين فإن ردت في اليوم لا يرتد بعد الغد، وقال زفر يبطل خيارها بعد غد أيضاً؛ لأنهما أمر واحد؛ لأنه عطف أحد الوقتين على الآخر تكرار لفظ الأمر، فيكون أمراً واحداً كما في الصورة الآتية أي اليوم وغداً، وكقوله: أنت طالق اليوم وبعد غد، قلنا: الأمر باليد يحتمل التوقيت لا حاجة إلى إدخال ما لم يدخل في اللفظ مقصوداً ولا تبعاً، فكانا أمرين ضرورة الانفصال، بخلاف الطلاق؛ لأنه لا يحتمل التوقيت فجاز أن يوصف في اليوم وبعد غد بطلاق واحد، فلا حاجة إلى إيقاع طلاق آخر ؛ لبقاء الأول إلى الوقت الثاني. وبخلاف قوله: "اليوم وغداً" على ما يأتي من الفرق أن الأمر باليد يحتمل التوقيت، فيتوقف الأمر بالأول ويجعل الثاني أمراً ابتداء، وعن أبي يوسف في الأمالي: " أنه إذا قال لامرأته : أمرك بيدك اليوم، وأمرك بيدك غداً إنهما أمران حتى إذا اختارت زوجها اليوم، ثم جاء الغد صار الأمر بيدها، وهو صحيح؛ لاستقلال كل واحد من الكلامين، فلا حاجة إلى الارتباط بما قبله، وينبغي أن يكون هذا بلا خلاف بينهم، ويتفرع عليه عدم جواز اختيارها نفسها ليلاً. (مستخلص، فتح) وكان الأمر بيدها بعد غد، وفي أمرك بيدك اليوم وغداً يدخل، وإن ردّت في أي المخيرة الأمر يومها لم يبق الأمر في الغد، ولو مكثت بعد التفويض يوماً ولم تقم، أو جلست في هذه المسألة بيدها أي المرأة المطلق عنه أو اتكأت عن قعود أو عكست أو دعت أباها للمشورة. أي عن القيام بأن كانت متكتة فقعدت أي طلبت أو أكثر و برد أحدهما لا يرد غد: لأنهما أمران لانفصال وقتهما فثبت لها الخيار في كل واحد من الوقتين على حدة الآخر. (ع) وفي أمرك أي في قوله لامرأته : أمرك إلخ. (ط) يدخل [ أي الليل في ذلك ويكون وقت الاختيار ممتدا إلى غروب الشمس من الغد. (ط)] أي يدخل الليل في قوله لها : أمرك بيدك اليوم وغدا؛ لأنه لم يتخلل بين الوقتين وقت من جنسهما لم يتناوله للأمر، فكان أمراً واحداً فإن قلت اليوم ههنا ذكر مفرداً فوجب أن يتناول الليل كالمسألة الأولى؟ قلت الجمع بينهما بحرف الجمع وهو الواو كالجمع بلفظة الجمع، فصار كقوله: "أمرك بيدك يومين" ولا يمكن ذلك في المسألة الأولى إلى اليوم وبعد غد؛ لتخلل وقت من جنسهما وهو الغد لم يدخل تحت اللفظ، وههنا أمكن؛ لعدم التخلل حتى لو قال هناك أيضاً أمرك بيدك اليوم وغداً وبعد غد كان أمراً واحداً للاتصال. [رمز الحقائق: ٢٤٩/١] (فتح) 11 لم يبق الأمر في الغد: لأنه أمر واحد، فلا يبقى لها الخيار بعد الرد كما إذا قال لها: أمرك بيدك اليوم فردته في أول النهار لا يبقى لها الخيار في آخره، وعن أبي حنيفة أنها إذا ردت الأمر في اليوم لها أن تختار نفسها غدا؛ لأنها لا تملك رد الأمر كما لا تملك رد الإيقاع، والجامع عدم اشتراط القبول فيهما في المجلس فصار بمنزلة قيامها عن المجلس، واشتغالها بعمل آخر وجه الظاهر أن المدة كلها بمنزلة المجلس فيما لم يذكر الوقت فيه؛ لكونه أمراً واحداً، وهناك لم يثبت لها الخيار بعد الرد فكذا هنا؛ ولأن من له الخيار بين شيئين إذا اختار أحدهما لا يكون له خيار الآخر، ألا تری أنها لو اختارت نفسها اليوم ليس لها أن تختار زوجها غداً فكذا هذا، وعن محمد: لو قال لامرأته: "أمرك بيدك "اليوم كان لها الخيار إلى غروب الشمس، ولو قال: أمرك بيدك في اليوم" كان لها الخيار في المجلس، فإذا قامت بطل، وهو كقوله : أنت طالق غداً وفي غد تبيين الحقائق: ٩٣/٣] (فتح) ولم تقم ولم تأخذ في عمل آخر. (ط)] المراد بالقيام المنفي ما يدل على الإعراض لا خصوص القيام، وهذا إذا كان التفويض مطلقاً، وأما إذا كان مؤقتاً فلا يبطل بالقيام ونحوه، وإنما يبطل الخيار بمضي الوقت وإن لم تقم، وإنما قيد بقوله : " لم تقم"؛ لأنها إذا قامت أو أخذت في عمل آخر خرج الأمر يدها كما مر، وقوله: "للمشورة" قال في المصباح شاورته واستشرته والاسم المشورة وفيها لغتان سكون الشين وفتح الواو، وضم الشين وسكون الواو، نقل الحموي أن المشورة بوزن المعونة هي اللغة الفصيحة الصحيحة، وفيها لغة أخرى مشورة كقسورة. (فتح) للمشورة بفتح الميم وضم الشين وفتح الراء وهي المشاورة. (ع) من
Book of Divorce. Ruling of the command by hand: they fall [three?]. And in 'I divorced myself with one' or 'I chose myself with a divorce', she becomes irrevocably divorced by one. And the night does not enter in 'your command is in your hand today and the day after tomorrow'. And if she rejects the command on her day, the command of that day is nullified. As for the woman given choice in the mentioned issue: 'they fall' means three because he intended [that is, his speech permits it]. And in 'I divorced myself' means in her reply to the husband when he said 'your command is in your hand'. 'With one' is an adjective for an omitted accusative source noun, i.e., I divorced myself with one divorce. 'She becomes irrevocably divorced by one' because the consideration is the husband's delegation, not her execution. In the two issues: the first: if the husband said to her 'your command is in your hand' and intended three, and she said in reply 'I divorced myself with one', then she is irrevocably divorced by one because 'one' is an adjective for an omitted source noun. And the second: if he said to her 'your command is in your hand' and intended three, and she said in reply 'I chose myself with a divorce', also by one, because in her reply there is explicit mention of a divorce which cannot be except one, and it is only irrevocable because the consideration is the husband's delegation, not her execution, so the mentioned adjective in the delegation is necessary in the reply for agreement. The intention of three in his saying 'your command is in your hand' is valid because the command by hand is a granting of ownership, so he owns granting what he owns, by analogy and juristic preference, unlike choice because divorce occurs by it contrary to analogy due to the consensus of the Companions, so it is constrained. And the mention of 'myself' in her saying 'I divorced myself' in reply to the command by hand is a condition: if he said to her 'your command is in your hand' and she said 'I divorced' without saying 'myself', nothing occurs. The night does not enter because each of the two days is mentioned individually, and the individual day does not include the night, unlike days because they include the nights corresponding to them. And 'the day after tomorrow': so she has no choice at night, and if she chose herself at night, divorce does not occur. The command of that day is nullified because he explicitly mentioned two times—today and the day after tomorrow—and between them there is a time, which is tomorrow, not covered by the command, so it is known that the mention of the second time was not meant to extend the first command, thus necessarily entailing a separate command. Since they are two commands, she has a choice in each of the two times; if she rejects on the first day, she does not lose the option for the day after tomorrow. Zufar said: her choice for the day after tomorrow is also nullified because they are one command due to the conjunction of one time to the other and the repetition of the word 'command', so it is one command as in the subsequent case (i.e., today and tomorrow) and like his saying 'you are divorced today and the day after tomorrow'. We said: the command by hand is susceptible to temporal specification; there is no need to include what is not included in the wording intentionally or incidentally, so they are two commands by necessity of separation, unlike divorce because it is not susceptible to temporal specification, so it is permissible for it to be described in 'today and the day after tomorrow' as one divorce; there is no need to effect another divorce because the first remains until the second time. And unlike his saying 'today and tomorrow', as the difference will come: that the command by hand is susceptible to temporal specification, so the first command is suspended and the second is made an initial command. And from Abu Yusuf in al-Amali: that if he said to his wife 'your command is in your hand today, and your command is in your hand tomorrow', they are two commands, so if she chooses her husband today, then when tomorrow comes, the command is in her hand, and this is correct because each statement is independent, so there is no need for connection to what preceded. And it should be that this is without disagreement among them, and it follows from it that she is not allowed to choose herself at night. The command is in her hand after the day after tomorrow. And in 'your command is in your hand today and tomorrow', it enters. And if she rejects the command on her day, the command does not remain for tomorrow. And if she remains after the delegation for a day without standing, or sits—in this issue, 'in her hand' means the woman from whom the divorce is being sought—or leans from sitting, or reverses, or calls her father for consultation. The negation of standing refers to what indicates disinterest, not specifically standing. And this is when the delegation is absolute; if it is time-bound, it is not nullified by standing and the like; rather, the choice is nullified by the passing of time even if she does not stand. And it is restricted by 'she did not stand' because when she stands or engages in another act, the command leaves her hand as previously mentioned. And his saying 'for consultation'—in al-Misbah: shawartuhu and istashartu, and the noun is mashwarah, with two dialects: sukun of shin and fatha of waw, and damm of shin and sukun of waw. al-Hamawi transmitted that ma-shu-ra (like ma'oona) is the eloquent correct dialect, and another dialect is mashurah like qaswurah. For consultation: with fatha of mim, damm of shin, and fatha of ra, and it is the same as mashawarah.
Source pages p. 427

Commentary
This passage from Kanzuldaqaiq discusses the rulings on the husband delegating the power of divorce to the wife (amr bil-yad). The text first addresses the effect of the husband's intention when delegating. If the husband intends three divorces but the wife responds with 'I divorce myself with one' or 'I choose myself with a single divorce', only one irrevocable divorce (ba'in) occurs. This is because the decisive factor is the husband's delegation, not the wife's execution; her response must match the delegation. The husband's intention of three is validated by the principle that amr bil-yad is a form of tamlik (granting ownership), so he can grant what he owns, based on qiyas and istihsan. The mention of 'nafsi' (myself) is a condition—if she omits it, no divorce occurs. Next, the text rules on time specifications. When the husband says 'today and the day after tomorrow', the night period between them is not included, and she cannot choose at night. Each day is a separate command, so if she rejects on the first day, her option for the second remains. Zufar disagrees, considering them one command, but the Hanafi position is that they are separate because amr bil-yad can be temporally specified. Abu Yusuf's view from al-Amali supports this. When the husband says 'today and tomorrow' without 'after', the night is included, and it is a single command. Rejection on the first day nullifies the option for the next day. Lastly, the text discusses the effect of the wife's actions after delegation. If she remains seated without standing or engaging in another activity, her option continues. Standing or starting another task indicates disinterest and nullifies the option. This applies to absolute delegation; if time-bound, only the expiry of time nullifies it. Consulting her father for advice does not nullify the option.

Key Terms
التوقيت (al-tawqit): Temporal specification; the ability to restrict a command to a specific time.
بعد غد (ba'da ghad): The day after tomorrow.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A husband says 'your command is in your hand today and tomorrow'. She rejects on the first day. Does she have an option on the next day?
A) Yes, because each day is separate
B) No, because it is one command
C) Yes, if she did not explicitly reject
D) No, because rejection nullifies everything

Key Takeaway
'Today and after tomorrow' are two separate commands; 'today and tomorrow' is one continuous command, due to the presence or absence of an intervening time.
