Talaq — Divorce
beginner
8 min
The Wife's Conduct After Delegation: When Does the Option Lapse?
Rulings on the wife's conduct after delegation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the actions that nullify the wife's option after amr bil-yad and distinguish between absolute and time-bound delegation.

Core Idea
The option continues while the wife remains in the same session; standing or engaging in another act indicates disinterest and nullifies it.

After receiving delegated authority, the wife must exercise her choice without indication of rejection. Standing up, starting another task, or engaging in a new activity is taken as disinterest, nullifying the option. However, consulting her father for advice does not nullify it. If the delegation is time-bound, only the expiry of time nullifies the option.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default rule
The wife's option remains valid as long as she stays in the same session without indicating disinterest. The text mentions 'remaining without standing' as the baseline.
The delegation is absolute when no time limit is set.
2
Define 'standing' as disinterest
Standing (qiyam) is not literal; any action that shows she is no longer deliberating, such as starting a new activity, is considered standing. If she stands or begins a different task, her option lapses.
The text explicitly says 'standing' but includes similar acts like leaning and reversing.
3
Identify exceptions to nullification
Consulting her father (or someone for advice) is not considered disinterest. Therefore, it does not nullify the option. Also, if the delegation is time-bound, only the expiry of the time nullifies it, not her actions.
The text says 'calling her father for consultation' does not nullify.
4
Apply to time-bound delegation
If the husband sets a specific time (e.g., 'today'), the option continues until the end of that period, regardless of standing or other actions.
Muhammad's view: if the husband says 'your command is in your hand today', the option lasts until sunset; if he says 'in the day', it lasts only in the sitting session.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطلاق حكم الأمر باليد وقعن، وفي طلقت نفسي بواحدة أو اخترتُ نفسي بتطليقةٍ بانت بواحدة، ولا يدخل الليل في أمرُك بيدك اليوم وبعد غد، وإن ردّت الأمر في يومها بطل أمر ذلك اليوم، تبين أي المرأة المخيرة في المسألة المذكورة وقعن: أي الثلاث؛ لأنه نوى محتمل كلامه (ع) وفي طلقت أي في قولها في جواب الزوج لما قال لها: أمرك بيدك. (ع) بواحدة: صفة لمصدر محذوف أي طلقت نفسي بتطليقة واحدة(ع) بانت بواحدة: [لأن الاعتبار بتفويض الزوج لا إيقاعها. (ع)] أي في المسألتين، أما الأولى : يعني لو قال الزوج لها: أمرك بيدك ونوى به ثلاثاً فقالت في جوابه: طلقت نفسي بواحدة فتبين بواحدة؛ لأن الواحدة صفة لمصدر محذوف تقديره طلقت نفسي بطلقة واحدة، وفي الثانية: أي لو قال لها: أمرك بيدك ونوى به ثلاثاً فقالت في جوابه: اخترت نفسي بتطليقة أيضاً بواحدة؛ لأن في جوابها تصريحا بالتطليقة وهي لا تكون إلا واحدة وإنما تكون بائنة؛ لأن المعتبر تفويض الزوج لا إيقاعها فتكون الصفة المذكورة في التفويض مذكورة في الجواب ضرورة الموافقة. وإنما صحت نية الثلاث في قوله: "أمرك بيدك"؛ لأن الأمر باليد تمليك فيملك تمليك ما يملكه قياسا واستحساناً، بخلاف التخيير؛ لأن وقوع الطلاق به على خلاف القياس لإجماع الصحابة فكان ضروريا، وذكر النفس في قولها: طلقت نفسي" في جواب الأمر باليد شرط حتى لو قال لها : أمرك بيدك فقالت: طلقت ولم تقل: نفسي لم يقع شيء. (مستخلص، فتح) ولا يدخل الليل لأن كل واحد من اليومين ذكر مفرداً، واليوم المفرد لا يتناول الليل، بخلاف الأيام؛ لأنها ينتظم ما بإزائها من الليالي مستخلص) وبعد غد فلا يكون لها الخيار بالليل حتى لو اختارت نفسها في الليل لا يقع الطلاق. (مص) من غير بطل أمر ذلك اليوم لأنه صرح بذكر وقتين اليوم وبعد غد أن بينهما وقت وهو الغد لم يتناول الأمر فعلم أنه ليس المراد بذكر الوقت الثاني امتداد الأمر الأول فاقتضى ضرورة إيجاب أمر آخر، فلما كانا أمرين ثبت لها الخيار في كل من الوقتين فإن ردت في اليوم لا يرتد بعد الغد، وقال زفر يبطل خيارها بعد غد أيضاً؛ لأنهما أمر واحد؛ لأنه عطف أحد الوقتين على الآخر تكرار لفظ الأمر، فيكون أمراً واحداً كما في الصورة الآتية أي اليوم وغداً، وكقوله: أنت طالق اليوم وبعد غد، قلنا: الأمر باليد يحتمل التوقيت لا حاجة إلى إدخال ما لم يدخل في اللفظ مقصوداً ولا تبعاً، فكانا أمرين ضرورة الانفصال، بخلاف الطلاق؛ لأنه لا يحتمل التوقيت فجاز أن يوصف في اليوم وبعد غد بطلاق واحد، فلا حاجة إلى إيقاع طلاق آخر ؛ لبقاء الأول إلى الوقت الثاني. وبخلاف قوله: "اليوم وغداً" على ما يأتي من الفرق أن الأمر باليد يحتمل التوقيت، فيتوقف الأمر بالأول ويجعل الثاني أمراً ابتداء، وعن أبي يوسف في الأمالي: " أنه إذا قال لامرأته : أمرك بيدك اليوم، وأمرك بيدك غداً إنهما أمران حتى إذا اختارت زوجها اليوم، ثم جاء الغد صار الأمر بيدها، وهو صحيح؛ لاستقلال كل واحد من الكلامين، فلا حاجة إلى الارتباط بما قبله، وينبغي أن يكون هذا بلا خلاف بينهم، ويتفرع عليه عدم جواز اختيارها نفسها ليلاً. (مستخلص، فتح) وكان الأمر بيدها بعد غد، وفي أمرك بيدك اليوم وغداً يدخل، وإن ردّت في أي المخيرة الأمر يومها لم يبق الأمر في الغد، ولو مكثت بعد التفويض يوماً ولم تقم، أو جلست في هذه المسألة بيدها أي المرأة المطلق عنه أو اتكأت عن قعود أو عكست أو دعت أباها للمشورة. أي عن القيام بأن كانت متكتة فقعدت أي طلبت أو أكثر و برد أحدهما لا يرد غد: لأنهما أمران لانفصال وقتهما فثبت لها الخيار في كل واحد من الوقتين على حدة الآخر. (ع) وفي أمرك أي في قوله لامرأته : أمرك إلخ. (ط) يدخل [ أي الليل في ذلك ويكون وقت الاختيار ممتدا إلى غروب الشمس من الغد. (ط)] أي يدخل الليل في قوله لها : أمرك بيدك اليوم وغدا؛ لأنه لم يتخلل بين الوقتين وقت من جنسهما لم يتناوله للأمر، فكان أمراً واحداً فإن قلت اليوم ههنا ذكر مفرداً فوجب أن يتناول الليل كالمسألة الأولى؟ قلت الجمع بينهما بحرف الجمع وهو الواو كالجمع بلفظة الجمع، فصار كقوله: "أمرك بيدك يومين" ولا يمكن ذلك في المسألة الأولى إلى اليوم وبعد غد؛ لتخلل وقت من جنسهما وهو الغد لم يدخل تحت اللفظ، وههنا أمكن؛ لعدم التخلل حتى لو قال هناك أيضاً أمرك بيدك اليوم وغداً وبعد غد كان أمراً واحداً للاتصال. [رمز الحقائق: ٢٤٩/١] (فتح) 11 لم يبق الأمر في الغد: لأنه أمر واحد، فلا يبقى لها الخيار بعد الرد كما إذا قال لها: أمرك بيدك اليوم فردته في أول النهار لا يبقى لها الخيار في آخره، وعن أبي حنيفة أنها إذا ردت الأمر في اليوم لها أن تختار نفسها غدا؛ لأنها لا تملك رد الأمر كما لا تملك رد الإيقاع، والجامع عدم اشتراط القبول فيهما في المجلس فصار بمنزلة قيامها عن المجلس، واشتغالها بعمل آخر وجه الظاهر أن المدة كلها بمنزلة المجلس فيما لم يذكر الوقت فيه؛ لكونه أمراً واحداً، وهناك لم يثبت لها الخيار بعد الرد فكذا هنا؛ ولأن من له الخيار بين شيئين إذا اختار أحدهما لا يكون له خيار الآخر، ألا تری أنها لو اختارت نفسها اليوم ليس لها أن تختار زوجها غداً فكذا هذا، وعن محمد: لو قال لامرأته: "أمرك بيدك "اليوم كان لها الخيار إلى غروب الشمس، ولو قال: أمرك بيدك في اليوم" كان لها الخيار في المجلس، فإذا قامت بطل، وهو كقوله : أنت طالق غداً وفي غد تبيين الحقائق: ٩٣/٣] (فتح) ولم تقم ولم تأخذ في عمل آخر. (ط)] المراد بالقيام المنفي ما يدل على الإعراض لا خصوص القيام، وهذا إذا كان التفويض مطلقاً، وأما إذا كان مؤقتاً فلا يبطل بالقيام ونحوه، وإنما يبطل الخيار بمضي الوقت وإن لم تقم، وإنما قيد بقوله : " لم تقم"؛ لأنها إذا قامت أو أخذت في عمل آخر خرج الأمر يدها كما مر، وقوله: "للمشورة" قال في المصباح شاورته واستشرته والاسم المشورة وفيها لغتان سكون الشين وفتح الواو، وضم الشين وسكون الواو، نقل الحموي أن المشورة بوزن المعونة هي اللغة الفصيحة الصحيحة، وفيها لغة أخرى مشورة كقسورة. (فتح) للمشورة بفتح الميم وضم الشين وفتح الراء وهي المشاورة. (ع) من
Book of Divorce. Ruling of the command by hand: they fall [three?]. And in 'I divorced myself with one' or 'I chose myself with a divorce', she becomes irrevocably divorced by one. And the night does not enter in 'your command is in your hand today and the day after tomorrow'. And if she rejects the command on her day, the command of that day is nullified. As for the woman given choice in the mentioned issue: 'they fall' means three because he intended [that is, his speech permits it]. And in 'I divorced myself' means in her reply to the husband when he said 'your command is in your hand'. 'With one' is an adjective for an omitted accusative source noun, i.e., I divorced myself with one divorce. 'She becomes irrevocably divorced by one' because the consideration is the husband's delegation, not her execution. In the two issues: the first: if the husband said to her 'your command is in your hand' and intended three, and she said in reply 'I divorced myself with one', then she is irrevocably divorced by one because 'one' is an adjective for an omitted source noun. And the second: if he said to her 'your command is in your hand' and intended three, and she said in reply 'I chose myself with a divorce', also by one, because in her reply there is explicit mention of a divorce which cannot be except one, and it is only irrevocable because the consideration is the husband's delegation, not her execution, so the mentioned adjective in the delegation is necessary in the reply for agreement. The intention of three in his saying 'your command is in your hand' is valid because the command by hand is a granting of ownership, so he owns granting what he owns, by analogy and juristic preference, unlike choice because divorce occurs by it contrary to analogy due to the consensus of the Companions, so it is constrained. And the mention of 'myself' in her saying 'I divorced myself' in reply to the command by hand is a condition: if he said to her 'your command is in your hand' and she said 'I divorced' without saying 'myself', nothing occurs. The night does not enter because each of the two days is mentioned individually, and the individual day does not include the night, unlike days because they include the nights corresponding to them. And 'the day after tomorrow': so she has no choice at night, and if she chose herself at night, divorce does not occur. The command of that day is nullified because he explicitly mentioned two times—today and the day after tomorrow—and between them there is a time, which is tomorrow, not covered by the command, so it is known that the mention of the second time was not meant to extend the first command, thus necessarily entailing a separate command. Since they are two commands, she has a choice in each of the two times; if she rejects on the first day, she does not lose the option for the day after tomorrow. Zufar said: her choice for the day after tomorrow is also nullified because they are one command due to the conjunction of one time to the other and the repetition of the word 'command', so it is one command as in the subsequent case (i.e., today and tomorrow) and like his saying 'you are divorced today and the day after tomorrow'. We said: the command by hand is susceptible to temporal specification; there is no need to include what is not included in the wording intentionally or incidentally, so they are two commands by necessity of separation, unlike divorce because it is not susceptible to temporal specification, so it is permissible for it to be described in 'today and the day after tomorrow' as one divorce; there is no need to effect another divorce because the first remains until the second time. And unlike his saying 'today and tomorrow', as the difference will come: that the command by hand is susceptible to temporal specification, so the first command is suspended and the second is made an initial command. And from Abu Yusuf in al-Amali: that if he said to his wife 'your command is in your hand today, and your command is in your hand tomorrow', they are two commands, so if she chooses her husband today, then when tomorrow comes, the command is in her hand, and this is correct because each statement is independent, so there is no need for connection to what preceded. And it should be that this is without disagreement among them, and it follows from it that she is not allowed to choose herself at night. The command is in her hand after the day after tomorrow. And in 'your command is in your hand today and tomorrow', it enters. And if she rejects the command on her day, the command does not remain for tomorrow. And if she remains after the delegation for a day without standing, or sits—in this issue, 'in her hand' means the woman from whom the divorce is being sought—or leans from sitting, or reverses, or calls her father for consultation. The negation of standing refers to what indicates disinterest, not specifically standing. And this is when the delegation is absolute; if it is time-bound, it is not nullified by standing and the like; rather, the choice is nullified by the passing of time even if she does not stand. And it is restricted by 'she did not stand' because when she stands or engages in another act, the command leaves her hand as previously mentioned. And his saying 'for consultation'—in al-Misbah: shawartuhu and istashartu, and the noun is mashwarah, with two dialects: sukun of shin and fatha of waw, and damm of shin and sukun of waw. al-Hamawi transmitted that ma-shu-ra (like ma'oona) is the eloquent correct dialect, and another dialect is mashurah like qaswurah. For consultation: with fatha of mim, damm of shin, and fatha of ra, and it is the same as mashawarah.
Source pages p. 427

Commentary
This passage from Kanzuldaqaiq discusses the rulings on the husband delegating the power of divorce to the wife (amr bil-yad). The text first addresses the effect of the husband's intention when delegating. If the husband intends three divorces but the wife responds with 'I divorce myself with one' or 'I choose myself with a single divorce', only one irrevocable divorce (ba'in) occurs. This is because the decisive factor is the husband's delegation, not the wife's execution; her response must match the delegation. The husband's intention of three is validated by the principle that amr bil-yad is a form of tamlik (granting ownership), so he can grant what he owns, based on qiyas and istihsan. The mention of 'nafsi' (myself) is a condition—if she omits it, no divorce occurs. Next, the text rules on time specifications. When the husband says 'today and the day after tomorrow', the night period between them is not included, and she cannot choose at night. Each day is a separate command, so if she rejects on the first day, her option for the second remains. Zufar disagrees, considering them one command, but the Hanafi position is that they are separate because amr bil-yad can be temporally specified. Abu Yusuf's view from al-Amali supports this. When the husband says 'today and tomorrow' without 'after', the night is included, and it is a single command. Rejection on the first day nullifies the option for the next day. Lastly, the text discusses the effect of the wife's actions after delegation. If she remains seated without standing or engaging in another activity, her option continues. Standing or starting another task indicates disinterest and nullifies the option. This applies to absolute delegation; if time-bound, only the expiry of time nullifies it. Consulting her father for advice does not nullify the option.

Key Terms
الإعراض (al-i'rad): Disinterest; actions indicating she is no longer deliberating, such as standing or starting another task.
المشورة (al-mashwarah): Consultation; seeking advice from a third party, which does not nullify the option.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In absolute delegation, which of the following DOES NOT nullify the wife's option?
A) Standing up from her seat
B) Calling her father for advice
C) Starting to read a book
D) Leaving the room

Key Takeaway
The wife's option remains valid unless she indicates disinterest through actions like standing; seeking advice does not nullify it, and time-bound delegation only ends by expiry of time.

The Option Period: Continuous or Discontinuous?
Ruling on the inclusion of the night in 'today and tomorrow'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that when a husband says 'your affair is in your hand today and tomorrow', the option period includes the night and is continuous, and explain the qiyas (analogy) to 'two days' that supports this ruling.

Core Idea
Today and tomorrow form one continuous option period, like saying 'two days'.

In this lesson, we examine a key scenario in the wife's delegated authority: when the husband specifies a time period using 'today and tomorrow.' The passage explains that this phrase creates a single, uninterrupted option period that includes the night between them, and it uses qiyas (analogy) to the case of 'two days' to justify this.

Guided Path
1
Identify the husband's phrasing
The husband says 'amruki bi-yadiki al-yawma wa ghadan' (your affair is in your hand today and tomorrow). This is the scenario under discussion.
2
Understand the ruling
The ruling states that the night between today and tomorrow is included, making the option period continuous until sunset of the next day.
This is based on the principle that the period is one continuous unit.
3
Analyze the qiyas
The author compares this to saying 'amruki bi-yadiki yawmayn' (two days) which is clearly one continuous period. The conjunction 'wa' joins the two days into one unit, just like the plural form.
Qiyas jaliy: clear analogy.
4
Consider the objection
An objection is raised: if saying 'today' alone includes the night, why is it different here? The response is that in 'today and tomorrow,' the two are joined by 'wa' making them one unit, whereas 'today and after tomorrow' has an intervening day (tomorrow) that breaks continuity.
The objection highlights the need to distinguish consecutive days from non-consecutive ones.
5
Derive the ruling
Thus, the option period is one continuous period; the wife must decide before the end of the period. This is the Hanafi position on this phrasing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

لم يبق الأمر في الغد: لأنه أمر واحد، فلا يبقى لها الخيار بعد الرد كما إذا قال لها: أمرك بيدك اليوم فردته في أول النهار لا يبقى لها الخيار في آخره، وعن أبي حنيفة أنها إذا ردت الأمر في اليوم لها أن تختار نفسها غدا؛ لأنها لا تملك رد الأمر كما لا تملك رد الإيقاع، والجامع عدم اشتراط القبول فيهما في المجلس فصار بمنزلة قيامها عن المجلس، واشتغالها بعمل آخر وجه الظاهر أن المدة كلها بمنزلة المجلس فيما لم يذكر الوقت فيه؛ لكونه أمراً واحداً، وهناك لم يثبت لها الخيار بعد الرد فكذا هنا؛ ولأن من له الخيار بين شيئين إذا اختار أحدهما لا يكون له خيار الآخر، ألا تری أنها لو اختارت نفسها اليوم ليس لها أن تختار زوجها غداً فكذا هذا، وعن محمد: لو قال لامرأته: "أمرك بيدك "اليوم كان لها الخيار إلى غروب الشمس، ولو قال: أمرك بيدك في اليوم" كان لها الخيار في المجلس، فإذا قامت بطل، وهو كقوله : أنت طالق غداً وفي غد تبيين الحقائق: ٩٣/٣] (فتح) ولم تقم ولم تأخذ في عمل آخر. أو شهوداً للإشهاد أو كانت على دابة فوقفت بقي خيارها، وإن سارت لا، أي دعت والفلك كالبيت. أي السفينة و جريانه لا يبطل خيارها هي أو محل أي لا يبقي خيارها أو شهوداً للإشهاد [إذا لم يكن عندها من تشهده سواء تحولت من مكانها أو لا في الأصح. (ف)] وإنما لا يبطل التفويض بالاستشارة أو الإشهاد؛ لأن الاستشارة لتحري الصواب ولهذا أمر عليها عائشة لهما بمشاورة والديها قبل أن تجيبه، والإشهاد للتحرز عن الجحود فصارا دليل الإقبال ولم يكونا دليل الإعراض. (ط، ع)] لأنه لم يوجد منها ما يدل على الإعراض؛ ولهذا لم يبطل في ما لو نامت قاعدة حتى لو دعت بطعام فأكلت أو قامت أو اغتسلت أو امتشت أو اختضبت أو كانت قاعدة فاضطجعت بطل خيارها؛ لأنه دليل الإعراض وكذا لو كانت راكبة فنزلت أو تحولت إلى دابة أخرى، أو كانت نازلة فركبت ولا فرق بين أن يكون الزوج معها على الدابة أو في المحمل أو لا يكون. ثم هذا إذا كانت حاضرة فإن كانت غائبة يعتبر مجلس علمها فإن قلت: إنه عليه لم يقيد الخيار بالمجلس؛ لأنه قال لعائشة: "فلا تجيبني حتى تستأمري أبويك؛ لأن الاستشارة معهما لا تكون إلا بعد المشي إليهما، قلت: إن إجماع الصحابة حجة وقول الرسول ليس فيه دلالة على عدم التقييد بالمجلس؛ إذ يمكنها الاستشارة وهي في مجلسها ولئن سلمنا عدم التقييد يحمل على أنه عليها أثبت لها الخيار ممتدا وله ولاية أن يشرع الحكم مطلقا ومقيدا فكانت عائشة لها مخصوصة بامتداد الخيار إلى الاستشارة. (عيني، فتح) وإن سارت لا: أي وإن سارت الدابة لا يبقى خيارها؛ لأن سيرها مضاف إليها لأن الدابة تسير باختيار راكبها فكأنها قامت عن المجلس، بخلاف الوقوف فإنه وإن كان بإيقافها؛ لكنه إقبال لا إعراض. (مستخلص، فتح والفلك كالبيت أي وإن كانا في السفينة فقال لها: أمرك بيدك ولم تقم وجرى السفينة لا يكون إعراضاً ولا يبطل خيارها؛ لأن السفينة بمنزلة البيت وسيرها غير مضاف إلى راكبها؛ لعدم قدرته على الإيقاف والتسيير فيثبت لها الخيار ما دامت في مجلسها، فإن تحولت بطل كما في البيت، وعن أبي يوسف: أن السفينة إذا كانت واقفة فسارت بطل خيارها. (مستخلص)
The Book of Divorce. Ruling on the authority being in her hand. If the authority was in her hand after tomorrow, and if he says 'your affair is in your hand today and tomorrow' it enters, and if she rejects in any day the option does not remain for tomorrow. And if she remains after delegation a day without standing, or she sits... etc. Commentary: meaning standing... etc.
Source pages p. 428

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the rulings of 'al-amr bi al-yad' (the wife's delegated authority to divorce herself). It begins by presenting the base text (matn) which lists several scenarios: when the husband says 'your affair is in your hand after tomorrow', 'today and tomorrow', and cases where the wife rejects or remains without standing. The commentary then expands each scenario. The first major sub-ruling discusses when the husband says 'today and tomorrow' – the night between them is included, making it one continuous option period until sunset of the next day. This is proven by analogy to saying 'two days' where the period is continuous. An objection is raised that 'today' alone would include the night, so why is it different here? The response is that the conjunction 'wa' joins them into one continuous period. The second part discusses the effect of the wife rejecting the option on a given day. The position of the author is that once she rejects, she loses the option for the next day because it is one continuous option. Abu Hanifa holds that she can still choose the next day because she cannot reject the option like she cannot reject the execution of divorce. The commentary then discusses that the entire period is like a session (majlis) for option purposes. The third part discusses the meaning of 'not standing' – it means not showing disinterest (i'rad). If the husband delegates absolutely, standing or similar actions end the option; if it is time-bound, only the expiry of time ends it. The fourth part discusses actions that do not indicate i'rad, such as consulting or summoning witnesses, as they show interest. Riding a stopped animal preserves the option, but walking on or moving the animal ends it because the movement is attributed to the rider. A ship is like a house – its movement does not end the option because the rider cannot control it; but Abu Yusuf held that if it moves from a stopped state, the option ends. The passage ends with the ruling that if the woman is present, the session is her location; if absent, the session of her knowledge is considered.

Key Terms
المخيرة (al-mukhayyara): The wife who is given the option to divorce herself.
اليوم وغداً (al-yawma wa ghadan): Today and tomorrow; a consecutive two-day period.
الليل (al-layl): The night between today and tomorrow.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when the husband says 'your affair is in your hand today and tomorrow', what is the ruling on the night between?
A) The night is not included because each day is separate.
B) The night is included, making the option period continuous until sunset of the next day.
C) The night is included only if the wife consents.
D) The night is excluded because it is not part of 'today' or 'tomorrow'.

Key Takeaway
When the husband uses 'today and tomorrow' with the conjunction 'wa', the option is one continuous period including the night between.

Effect of Rejection on the Option: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on rejection of option

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position (majority view) that if the wife rejects the option on day one, she loses it for the next day, and explain the counter-argument of Abu Hanifa and the reasoning behind the tarjih.

Core Idea
Rejecting the option on day one ends it for the next day because the period is one unit.

This lesson addresses a critical intra-Hanafi dispute: if the wife is given the option for two days and she rejects it on the first day, does she still have the option on the second day? The passage presents the majority view (Muhammad and Abu Yusuf) that the option is lost, and the dissenting view of Imam Abu Hanifa that it remains. Understanding this dispute clarifies the nature of the option period as a single continuous unit.

Guided Path
1
State the issue
The wife is given the option for a period (e.g., two days). She explicitly rejects the option on the first day. Does she still have the option on the second day?
2
Identify the majority view
The author (following Muhammad and Abu Yusuf) holds that once she rejects, the option ends entirely. The period is one continuous unit like a session (majlis).
This is the mufta bihi position.
3
Understand Abu Hanifa's view
Abu Hanifa argues that she cannot 'reject' the option because she does not have the power to reject it; she can only accept or not. Analogy: she cannot reject the execution of divorce, so she cannot reject the option. The option thus continues to the next day.
This view gives the wife more flexibility.
4
Examine the Hanafi response
The majority responds that the period is like a session; after the session ends, the option is lost. Rejecting on day one is like leaving the session. Also, if she had chosen divorce on day one, she could not choose the husband on day two; similarly, rejecting is like choosing one side.
The response uses analogy to khiyar in a session.
5
Determine the practical consequence
Under the majority view, once she rejects, she cannot divorce herself later. Under Abu Hanifa's view, she can still divorce herself the next day. The fatwa follows the majority.

كتاب الطلاق
حكم الأمر باليد
وكان الأمر بيدها بعد غد، وفي أمرك بيدك اليوم وغداً يدخل، وإن ردّت في أي المخيرة الأمر يومها لم يبق الأمر في الغد، ولو مكثت بعد التفويض يوماً ولم تقم، أو جلست بيدها أي المرأة المطلق عنه أو اتكأت عن قعود أو عكست أو دعت أباها للمشورة. أي عن القيام بأن كانت متكتة فقعدت أي طلبت أو أكثر و برد أحدهما لا يرد غد: لأنهما أمران لانفصال وقتهما فثبت لها الخيار في كل واحد من الوقتين على حدة الآخر. (ع) وفي أمرك أي في قوله لامرأته : أمرك إلخ. (ط) يدخل [ أي الليل في ذلك ويكون وقت الاختيار ممتدا إلى غروب الشمس من الغد. (ط)] أي يدخل الليل في قوله لها : أمرك بيدك اليوم وغدا؛ لأنه لم يتخلل بين الوقتين وقت من جنسهما لم يتناوله للأمر، فكان أمراً واحداً فإن قلت اليوم ههنا ذكر مفرداً فوجب أن يتناول الليل كالمسألة الأولى؟ قلت الجمع بينهما بحرف الجمع وهو الواو كالجمع بلفظة الجمع، فصار كقوله: "أمرك بيدك يومين" ولا يمكن ذلك في المسألة الأولى إلى اليوم وبعد غد؛ لتخلل وقت من جنسهما وهو الغد لم يدخل تحت اللفظ، وههنا أمكن؛ لعدم التخلل حتى لو قال هناك أيضاً أمرك بيدك اليوم وغداً وبعد غد كان أمراً واحداً للاتصال.
لم يبق الأمر في الغد: لأنه أمر واحد، فلا يبقى لها الخيار بعد الرد كما إذا قال لها: أمرك بيدك اليوم فردته في أول النهار لا يبقى لها الخيار في آخره، وعن أبي حنيفة أنها إذا ردت الأمر في اليوم لها أن تختار نفسها غدا؛ لأنها لا تملك رد الأمر كما لا تملك رد الإيقاع، والجامع عدم اشتراط القبول فيهما في المجلس فصار بمنزلة قيامها عن المجلس، واشتغالها بعمل آخر وجه الظاهر أن المدة كلها بمنزلة المجلس فيما لم يذكر الوقت فيه؛ لكونه أمراً واحداً، وهناك لم يثبت لها الخيار بعد الرد فكذا هنا؛ ولأن من له الخيار بين شيئين إذا اختار أحدهما لا يكون له خيار الآخر، ألا تری أنها لو اختارت نفسها اليوم ليس لها أن تختار زوجها غداً فكذا هذا، وعن محمد: لو قال لامرأته: "أمرك بيدك "اليوم كان لها الخيار إلى غروب الشمس، ولو قال: أمرك بيدك في اليوم" كان لها الخيار في المجلس، فإذا قامت بطل، وهو كقوله : أنت طالق غداً وفي غد تبيين الحقائق: ٩٣/٣] (فتح) ولم تقم ولم تأخذ في عمل آخر. (ط)] المراد بالقيام المنفي ما يدل على الإعراض لا خصوص القيام، وهذا إذا كان التفويض مطلقاً، وأما إذا كان مؤقتاً فلا يبطل بالقيام ونحوه، وإنما يبطل الخيار بمضي الوقت وإن لم تقم.
وقوله: "للمشورة" قال في المصباح شاورته واستشرته والاسم المشورة وفيها لغتان سكون الشين وفتح الواو ، وضم الشين وسكون الواو، نقل الحموي أن المشورة بوزن المعونة هي اللغة الفصيحة الصحيحة، وفيها لغة أخرى مشورة كقسورة. (فتح) للمشورة بفتح الميم وضم الشين وفتح الراء وهي المشاورة. (ع)

كتاب الطلاق
حكم الأمر باليد
أو شهوداً للإشهاد أو كانت على دابة فوقفت بقي خيارها، وإن سارت لا، أي دعت والفلك كالبيت. أي السفينة و جريانه لا يبطل خيارها هي أو محل أي لا يبقي خيارها أو شهوداً للإشهاد [إذا لم يكن عندها من تشهده سواء تحولت من مكانها أو لا في الأصح. (ف)] وإنما لا يبطل التفويض بالاستشارة أو الإشهاد؛ لأن الاستشارة لتحري الصواب ولهذا أمر عليها عائشة لهما بمشاورة والديها قبل أن تجيبه، والإشهاد للتحرز عن الجحود فصارا دليل الإقبال ولم يكونا دليل الإعراض. (مستخلص، فتح) فوقفت أي الدابة وأوقفتها أو نزلت (ط، ع) بقي خيارها الأن هذه الأشياء ليست دليل الإعراض وهذا إذا كانت حاضرة فإن كانت غائبة يعتبر مجلس علمها. (ط، ع)] لأنه لم يوجد منها ما يدل على الإعراض؛ ولهذا لم يبطل في ما لو نامت قاعدة حتى لو دعت بطعام فأكلت أو قامت أو اغتسلت أو امتشت أو اختضبت أو كانت قاعدة فاضطجعت بطل خيارها؛ لأنه دليل الإعراض وكذا لو كانت راكبة فنزلت أو تحولت إلى دابة أخرى، أو كانت نازلة فركبت ولا فرق بين أن يكون الزوج معها على الدابة أو في المحمل أو لا يكون. ثم هذا إذا كانت حاضرة فإن كانت غائبة يعتبر مجلس علمها فإن قلت: إنه عليه لم يقيد الخيار بالمجلس؛ لأنه قال لعائشة: "فلا تجيبني حتى تستأمري أبويك؛ لأن الاستشارة معهما لا تكون إلا بعد المشي إليهما، قلت: إن إجماع الصحابة حجة وقول الرسول ليس فيه دلالة على عدم التقييد بالمجلس؛ إذ يمكنها الاستشارة وهي في مجلسها ولئن سلمنا عدم التقييد يحمل على أنه عليها أثبت لها الخيار ممتدا وله ولاية أن يشرع الحكم مطلقا ومقيدا فكانت عائشة لها مخصوصة بامتداد الخيار إلى الاستشارة. (عيني، فتح) وإن سارت لا: أي وإن سارت الدابة لا يبقى خيارها؛ لأن سيرها مضاف إليها لأن الدابة تسير باختيار راكبها فكأنها قامت عن المجلس، بخلاف الوقوف فإنه وإن كان بإيقافها؛ لكنه إقبال لا إعراض. (مستخلص، فتح والفلك كالبيت أي وإن كانا في السفينة فقال لها: أمرك بيدك ولم تقم وجرى السفينة لا يكون إعراضاً ولا يبطل خيارها؛ لأن السفينة بمنزلة البيت وسيرها غير مضاف إلى راكبها؛ لعدم قدرته على الإيقاف والتسيير فيثبت لها الخيار ما دامت في مجلسها، فإن تحولت بطل كما في البيت، وعن أبي يوسف: أن السفينة إذا كانت واقفة فسارت بطل خيارها. (مستخلص)
The Book of Divorce. Ruling on the authority being in her hand. If the authority was in her hand after tomorrow, and if he says 'your affair is in your hand today and tomorrow' it enters, and if she rejects in any day the option does not remain for tomorrow. And if she remains after delegation a day without standing, or she sits... etc. Commentary: meaning standing... etc.
Source pages p. 428

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the rulings of 'al-amr bi al-yad' (the wife's delegated authority to divorce herself). It begins by presenting the base text (matn) which lists several scenarios: when the husband says 'your affair is in your hand after tomorrow', 'today and tomorrow', and cases where the wife rejects or remains without standing. The commentary then expands each scenario. The first major sub-ruling discusses when the husband says 'today and tomorrow' – the night between them is included, making it one continuous option period until sunset of the next day. This is proven by analogy to saying 'two days' where the period is continuous. An objection is raised that 'today' alone would include the night, so why is it different here? The response is that the conjunction 'wa' joins them into one continuous period. The second part discusses the effect of the wife rejecting the option on a given day. The position of the author is that once she rejects, she loses the option for the next day because it is one continuous option. Abu Hanifa holds that she can still choose the next day because she cannot reject the option like she cannot reject the execution of divorce. The commentary then discusses that the entire period is like a session (majlis) for option purposes. The third part discusses the meaning of 'not standing' – it means not showing disinterest (i'rad). If the husband delegates absolutely, standing or similar actions end the option; if it is time-bound, only the expiry of time ends it. The fourth part discusses actions that do not indicate i'rad, such as consulting or summoning witnesses, as they show interest. Riding a stopped animal preserves the option, but walking on or moving the animal ends it because the movement is attributed to the rider. A ship is like a house – its movement does not end the option because the rider cannot control it; but Abu Yusuf held that if it moves from a stopped state, the option ends. The passage ends with the ruling that if the woman is present, the session is her location; if absent, the session of her knowledge is considered.

Key Terms
الرد (al-radd): The wife's explicit rejection of the option to divorce.
الخيار (al-khiyar): The option or choice given to the wife.
المجلس (al-majlis): The session where the option is given; used analogically for the period.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the main reason the majority (Muhammad and Abu Yusuf) give for the option ending upon rejection?
A) The wife cannot reject the option, so it continues.
B) The period is like a session, and rejection is like leaving the session.
C) The husband's delegation is automatically canceled upon rejection.
D) The wife must consult before rejecting.

Key Takeaway
The majority Hanafi view holds that rejecting the option on day one ends it for subsequent days because the period is a single continuous unit like a session.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
10 min
Actions that Invalidate the Option: I'rad and Exceptions
Detailed listing of actions that end or preserve the wife's option

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify actions that constitute i'rad (disinterest) and void the option, distinguish them from actions that preserve the option (e.g., consulting, calling witnesses), and apply the ruling to scenarios involving riding animals and ships.

Core Idea
Standing, walking, or similar actions void the option; consulting or calling witnesses do not.

This lesson covers the concept of i'rad (turning away) in the context of the wife's delegated authority. When a husband delegates the choice to his wife absolutely, her actions can indicate whether she is interested in exercising the option or not. The passage lists specific actions that are considered i'rad (voiding the option) and those that are not (preserving the option). Special rules apply to riding animals and ships.

Guided Path
1
Understand the principle of i'rad
I'rad means disinterest. If the wife engages in actions that show she is turning away from the option, the option is invalidated. The key is whether the action indicates i'rad, not the specific action itself.
2
Identify actions that indicate i'rad
Examples from the text: standing up, walking, eating, washing, combing hair, applying henna, lying down when previously sitting, dismounting from a riding animal, changing to another animal. These all show she is moving on.
3
Identify actions that do not indicate i'rad
Consulting (e.g., calling parents for advice) and calling witnesses for testimony are not i'rad because they show she is still considering the option or preserving her rights.
4
Apply the ruling to riding animals
If the wife is on a riding animal and it is stationary, her option remains. If the animal moves (she causes it to walk), the option ends because movement is attributed to her. Stopping the animal does not end the option.
5
Apply the ruling to ships
A ship is like a house; its movement does not end the option because the passenger cannot control it. However, if she moves within the ship (e.g., changes location), the option ends.
Abu Yusuf held different view: if the ship moves from stationary, option ends.

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the rulings of 'al-amr bi al-yad' (the wife's delegated authority to divorce herself). It begins by presenting the base text (matn) which lists several scenarios: when the husband says 'your affair is in your hand after tomorrow', 'today and tomorrow', and cases where the wife rejects or remains without standing. The commentary then expands each scenario. The first major sub-ruling discusses when the husband says 'today and tomorrow' – the night between them is included, making it one continuous option period until sunset of the next day. This is proven by analogy to saying 'two days' where the period is continuous. An objection is raised that 'today' alone would include the night, so why is it different here? The response is that the conjunction 'wa' joins them into one continuous period. The second part discusses the effect of the wife rejecting the option on a given day. The position of the author is that once she rejects, she loses the option for the next day because it is one continuous option. Abu Hanifa holds that she can still choose the next day because she cannot reject the option like she cannot reject the execution of divorce. The commentary then discusses that the entire period is like a session (majlis) for option purposes. The third part discusses the meaning of 'not standing' – it means not showing disinterest (i'rad). If the husband delegates absolutely, standing or similar actions end the option; if it is time-bound, only the expiry of time ends it. The fourth part discusses actions that do not indicate i'rad, such as consulting or summoning witnesses, as they show interest. Riding a stopped animal preserves the option, but walking on or moving the animal ends it because the movement is attributed to the rider. A ship is like a house – its movement does not end the option because the rider cannot control it; but Abu Yusuf held that if it moves from a stopped state, the option ends. The passage ends with the ruling that if the woman is present, the session is her location; if absent, the session of her knowledge is considered.

Key Terms
الإعراض (al-i'rad): Actions indicating disinterest that void the option.
المشورة (al-mashwara): Consultation; not considered i'rad.
الإشهاد (al-ishhad): Calling witnesses; not i'rad.
الفلك (al-fulk): Ship; movement does not end option.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following actions does NOT invalidate the wife's option when she is given absolute delegation?
A) Standing up and walking
B) Calling her father for advice
C) Bathing
D) Dismounting from a riding animal

Key Takeaway
Actions that indicate the wife is turning away (i'rad) void the absolute delegation; actions showing continued interest preserve it.

Talaq — Divorce
beginner
7 min
The Basic Ruling of Tamlik: One Revocable Divorce
Explains ruling when husband tells wife 'divorce yourself'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the legal effect when a husband says 'Tallaqi nafsik' without specifying a number, and the wife divorces once, and explain why it is one revocable divorce.

Core Idea
Delegating divorce yields one revocable divorce by default; the command is a genus applying to the minimum.

When a husband delegates the right to divorce to his wife by saying 'Divorce yourself,' he gives her authority to execute a divorce. The default ruling, if no number is intended, is that one revocable divorce takes place. This lesson unpacks that ruling and its rationale based on the nature of the command and the type of divorce.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and ruling
The husband says 'Tallaqi nafsik' without intending any specific number or intending one divorce. The wife then says 'I divorce myself' once. The ruling is that one revocable divorce occurs.
2
Locate the dalil (evidence) for the ruling
The passage explains that it is one because the command 'divorce yourself' is a generic term (ism jins) that applies to the minimum for certainty, similar to other generic nouns. It is revocable because the delegated power is over explicit divorce (sareeh), which is revocable.
The dalil is not a specific text but a linguistic and usul principle.
3
Note the conditions for this ruling
The wife must respond in the same session (implied from tamlik rules, though not explicit here) and the husband must not have intended a different number.
4
Contrast with other possibilities
If the husband intended three and she divorces three, they occur. If he intended two, there is a dispute, which will be covered in a later lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

أي في بيان حكم المشيئة

أي الزوج لامرأة
والحال أنه لم ينو شيئاً
أي طلقة واحدة
طلقت ثلاثاً ونواه وقعنَ وبأبنت نفسي طلقت لا باخترتُ، أي المرأة
فصل: أي في المشيئة اعلم أن المناسب للترجمة الابتداء بمسألة فيها ذكر المشيئة لكن ما ذكر فيه المشيئة منزل من ما لم تذكر فيه منزلة المركب من المفرد والمفرد يسبق المركب فكذا ما نزل منزله. (فتح)
ولم ينو أو نوى واحدة لو عكس العبارة بأن قال: "نوى واحدة أو لم ينو" أو اقتصر على قوله: "ولم ينو" لكان أولى؛ لأنه إذا طلقت واحدة مع عدم النية فمع نيتها بالأولى (فتح) فطلقت نفسها بأن قالت: طلقت نفسي. (ع) وقعت رجعية أما وقوع الطلاق؛ فلأنه ملكه إياها وأما كونه واحدة فلأنه أمر معناه افعلي فعل الطلاق، وهو جنس يقع على الأدنى للتيقن ويحتمل الكل عند الإرادة والنية كسائر أسماء الأجناس، وأما كونه رجعياً؛ فلأن المفوض إليها صريح الطلاق، وإنه معقب للرجعة. (ط)] أي والحال أن الزوج نوى الثلاث، وقيد المصنف بنية الثلاث؛ لأنه لو نوى واحدة لم يقع شيء عند أبي حنيفة، وعندهما يقع واحدة، وقوله : "وقعن؛ لأن قوله: "طلقي نفسك معناه افعلي فعل التطليق مقيد بخطابها، ولا فيه نية الثنتين؛ لأنه عدد محض لا يشمله المصدر إلا أن تكون المنكوحة أمة. (فتح، عيني) يصح وبأبنت: أي بقول المرأة بـ"أبنت نفسي في جواب قوله: طلقي نفسك. (ط،ع) طلقت لا باخترت [ أي لا تطلق لو قال لها: طلقي نفسك فأجابت بقولها: اخترت. (ط،ع)] أي لو قال لها: نفسك" فقالت في جوابه أبنت نفسي أو طلقت نفسي طلاقاً بائناً، طلقت رجعية؛ لأنها قالت في جواب "طلقي نفسك"، وهي صريح، فبطلت صفة الإبانة في الجواب وبقي مطلق الطلاق وهي رجعي، وهذا لما قلنا: إن الاعتبار لجانب التفويض، ولو قالت في جوابه اخترت نفسي، لا يقع شيء، وخرج الأمر من يدها، والفرق: أن
"طلقي
الإبانة من ألفاظ الطلاق التي تستعمل في إيقاعه كناية وقد أجابت بما فوض إليها غير أنها زادت فيه وصفاً فيلغو. بخلاف اخترت"؛ إذ الاختيار ليس من الصريح ولا من الكناية، ومن ثممه لا يقدر على إيقاع الطلاق به حتى إذا قال لها: "اخترتك" ينوي الطلاق لا يقع شيء، وأن وقوع الطلاق بـ"اخترت" على خلاف القياس عرف بإجماع الصحابة إذا كان جواباً للتخيير فيقتصر على مورده، وقوله: "طلقي" ليس بتخيير فيلغو، وعن أبي حنيفة أنه لا يقع بقولها: "أبنت نفسي" لأنها أتت بغير ما فوض إليها الطلاق والإبانة تخالفه فكان إعراضها منها، فيبطل خيارها به، ووجه الظاهر أن الإبانة من ألفاظ الطلاق وضعاً وحكماً فيقع، ولكنه رجعي لمخالفتها إياه في الوصف. (مستخلص، عيني، فتح)
Chapter: Explanation of the ruling of delegation. Meaning: in explanation of the ruling of delegation. And if he said to her: 'Divorce yourself' and he did not intend or intended one, and she divorced, it occurs as one revocable divorce. Meaning: the husband to the wife, and the state being that he did not intend anything. Meaning: one divorce. She divorced three and he intended them, they occur. And with 'I separated myself' she divorces, not with 'I chose.' Meaning: the woman. Chapter: Meaning regarding delegation: Know that it is appropriate for the title to begin with a matter in which delegation is mentioned, but that which is mentioned regarding delegation is given the status of a compound from a simple element, and the simple precedes the compound, so likewise that which is given its status. (Fath) And he did not intend or intended one: if he reversed the phrase by saying: 'intended one or did not intend' or limited himself to saying: 'and he did not intend,' it would be better; because if she divorces once with absence of intention, then with intention it is even more so. (Fath) Then she divorced herself by saying: 'I divorced myself.' (A) It occurs revocable. As for the occurrence of divorce: because he granted it to her. As for it being one: because his command means 'perform the act of divorce,' and it is a genus that applies to the minimum for certainty and can include all with intention and will, like other generic nouns. As for it being revocable: because what is delegated to her is explicit divorce, and it allows for return (رجعة). [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 2/250] Three: by her saying: 'I divorced myself three times.' (T) and he intended them, they occur. Meaning: the three; and if he intended two, his intention is not valid unless the woman is a slave. (T) Meaning: and the state being that the husband intended three. The author restricted it to intention for three because if he intended one, nothing occurs according to Abu Hanifa, while according to the two companions, one occurs. And his statement: 'they occur' because his saying 'divorce yourself' means 'perform the act of divorce' restricted to her address, and there is no intention for two in it because it is a pure number not included in the verbal noun unless the married woman is a slave. (Fath, 'Ayni) It is valid. And 'abantu': meaning the woman saying 'I separated myself' in response to his saying 'divorce yourself.' (T, A) She divorces, not with 'ikhtartu.' [Meaning: she does not divorce if he said to her 'divorce yourself' and she responded by saying 'I chose.' (T, A)] Meaning: if he said to her: 'divorce yourself' and she responded with 'I separated myself' or 'I divorced myself with an irrevocable divorce,' she divorces revocably; because she responded to 'divorce yourself,' which is explicit, so the description of irrevocability in her response is nullified and general divorce remains, which is revocable. This is because we said: consideration is given to the delegation side. And if she responded with 'I chose myself,' nothing occurs and the matter leaves her hand. The difference is that 'ibanah' (separation) is among the words of divorce used figuratively for its occurrence, and she has responded with what was delegated to her, but she added a description, so it is nullified. Contrary to 'ikhtartu'; because choice (ikhtiyar) is neither explicit nor figurative, and therefore divorce cannot be effected with it; even if he said to her 'I choose you' intending divorce, nothing occurs. And that occurrence of divorce with 'ikhtartu' is against analogy, known by the consensus of the Companions when it is a response to giving choice (takhyir), so it is confined to its context. And his statement 'divorce' is not giving choice, so it is nullified. And from Abu Hanifa: that it does not occur with her saying 'I separated myself' because she brought something other than what was delegated to her—divorce and separation are different—so it is her turning away, and thus her option is voided. But the apparent view is that 'ibanah' is from the words of divorce linguistically and legally, so it occurs, but it is revocable due to her opposing him in the description. (Mustakhlas, 'Ayni, Fath)
Source pages p. 430

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq with its commentary explains the ruling when a husband delegates the power to divorce to his wife by saying 'طلقي نفسك' (divorce yourself). The passage begins by stating that if the husband says this without any intention or with the intention of one divorce, and the wife then divorces herself once, it falls as a single revocable divorce. The commentary clarifies that the divorce is valid because the husband has granted the authority (tamlik). It is one divorce because the command 'divorce' is a generic term that applies to the minimum. It is revocable because the delegated power is over explicit divorce (sareeh), which is revocable. The passage then discusses the scenario where the wife divorces herself three times and the husband intended three: all three occur. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: if the husband intended two divorces, Abu Hanifa says nothing occurs, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say one divorce occurs. The correct view is that the intention for two is not valid unless the wife is a slave. Next, the passage examines the wife's response using the phrase 'أبنت نفسي' (I separated myself) versus 'اخترت نفسي' (I chose myself). If she says 'أبنت نفسي,' it is considered a revocable divorce because 'ibanah' is a kinayah for divorce and she has responded to the delegation, but her addition of the description of irrevocability is nullified. If she says 'اخترت نفسي,' nothing occurs because 'ikhtiyar' is not a term of divorce at all; the ruling for 'اخترت' in cases of takhyir is established by the consensus of the Companions and is limited to that context. There is also a report from Abu Hanifa that even 'أبنت' should not result in divorce, but the apparent view is that it does, but as revocable.

Key Terms
تمليك (tamlik): Delegation of the right to divorce to the wife by the husband, where he gives her authority to execute the divorce.
تفويض (tafwid): Empowerment of the wife to choose divorce or not, similar to tamlik.
صريح (sareeh): Explicit words of divorce that do not require intention, e.g., 'anti taliq'.
كناية (kinayah): Implicit words that can be used for divorce but also have other meanings, requiring intention for divorce to occur.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When a husband says 'Tallaqi nafsik' to his wife without any intention, and she divorces herself once, what is the result?
A) No divorce occurs
B) One irrevocable divorce
C) One revocable divorce
D) Two divorces

Key Takeaway
Delegation of divorce (tamlik) yields a single revocable divorce unless a specific number is intended and executed.

Talaq — Divorce

Intention for a Specific Number: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Two Divorces
Explains ruling when husband tells wife 'divorce yourself' – focusing on intention for specific numbers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the effect of the husband's intention for two divorces when he says 'Tallaqi nafsik', and state the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Intention for two divorces in tamlik is ineffective unless the wife is a slave; the Sahibayn's view that one revocable divorce occurs is mufta bihi for free women.

When a husband delegates divorce and intends a specific number, the effect depends on whether the number is encompassed by the generic command. The classic dispute arises when he intends two divorces and the wife performs one. Abu Hanifa and his two companions diverge on the outcome. This lesson dissects the arguments and the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
State the disputed issue
Husband says 'Tallaqi nafsik' intending two divorces. Wife divorces herself once. The question: does any divorce occur?
2
Identify the two positions
Abu Hanifa: no divorce occurs. Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): one revocable divorce occurs.
The passage also notes an exception: if the wife is a slave, the husband's intention for two is valid.
3
Analyze the dalil of each
Abu Hanifa: the command 'divorce yourself' is restricted by the husband's intention; since he intended two, she must do two. Her doing one means she did not follow the command, so nothing occurs. Sahibayn: the command is generic (ism jins) and applies to the minimum (one); the intention for a specific number (two) is a pure number not included in the verbal noun (masdar), so it is ineffective unless she actually performs two. Since she did one, it falls under the minimum.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: under Abu Hanifa, the marriage remains intact; under Sahibayn, one revocable divorce occurs, so the marriage is not dissolved but the couple can reconcile during iddah.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
The passage restricts the discussion to intention for three, implying that for intention for two, the relied-upon view is that of the Sahibayn, especially since the text says 'لا تصح نيته إلا أن تكون المرأة أمة' – his intention is not valid unless the wife is a slave, which aligns with the Sahibayn that only one divorce occurs.

Source pages p. 430

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq with its commentary explains the ruling when a husband delegates the power to divorce to his wife by saying 'طلقي نفسك' (divorce yourself). The passage begins by stating that if the husband says this without any intention or with the intention of one divorce, and the wife then divorces herself once, it falls as a single revocable divorce. The commentary clarifies that the divorce is valid because the husband has granted the authority (tamlik). It is one divorce because the command 'divorce' is a generic term that applies to the minimum. It is revocable because the delegated power is over explicit divorce (sareeh), which is revocable. The passage then discusses the scenario where the wife divorces herself three times and the husband intended three: all three occur. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: if the husband intended two divorces, Abu Hanifa says nothing occurs, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say one divorce occurs. The correct view is that the intention for two is not valid unless the wife is a slave. Next, the passage examines the wife's response using the phrase 'أبنت نفسي' (I separated myself) versus 'اخترت نفسي' (I chose myself). If she says 'أبنت نفسي,' it is considered a revocable divorce because 'ibanah' is a kinayah for divorce and she has responded to the delegation, but her addition of the description of irrevocability is nullified. If she says 'اخترت نفسي,' nothing occurs because 'ikhtiyar' is not a term of divorce at all; the ruling for 'اخترت' in cases of takhyir is established by the consensus of the Companions and is limited to that context. There is also a report from Abu Hanifa that even 'أبنت' should not result in divorce, but the apparent view is that it does, but as revocable.

Key Terms
تمليك (tamlik): Delegation of the right to divorce to the wife by the husband, where he gives her authority to execute the divorce.
عدد محض (adad mahd): A pure number, like two or three, that is not included in the generic verbal noun (masdar).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) No divorce occurs
B) Two divorces occur
C) One revocable divorce occurs
D) One irrevocable divorce occurs

Key Takeaway
In tamlik, the husband's intention for a specific number (like two) is ineffective unless the wife performs that number; the default is one revocable divorce.

Talaq — Divorce

The Wife's Response: 'Abantu Nafsi' vs 'Ikhtartu Nafsi'
Explains ruling when husband tells wife 'divorce yourself' – focusing on the wife's response phrases

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the rulings when the wife responds to 'Tallaqi nafsik' with 'abantu nafsi' versus 'ikhtartu nafsi', and explain why 'abantu' results in a revocable divorce.

Core Idea
‘Abantu nafsi’ is a kinayah for divorce and yields revocable divorce; ‘ikhtartu nafsi’ is not a divorce word and yields nothing.

When the husband delegates divorce, the wife's choice of words in response matters. Saying 'I separated myself' (أبنت نفسي) is considered a kinayah for divorce and results in a revocable divorce, whereas saying 'I chose myself' (اخترت نفسي) does not effect divorce at all. This lesson explores the reasoning behind these rulings and a reported difference from Abu Hanifa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The husband says 'Tallaqi nafsik'. The wife responds either with 'Abantu nafsi' (I separated myself) or 'Ikhtartu nafsi' (I chose myself).
2
Ruling for 'abantu nafsi'
The apparent view (وجه الظاهر) is that a revocable divorce occurs. This is because 'ibanah' (separation) is a kinayah for divorce, and she responded to the delegation. Any description of irrevocability she adds is nullified, leaving a revocable divorce.
There is a report from Abu Hanifa that no divorce occurs, but the apparent view is preferred.
3
Ruling for 'ikhtartu nafsi'
No divorce occurs, and the matter leaves her hand. This is because 'ikhtiyar' (choice) is not a term for divorce at all; it cannot effect divorce even if intended. The ruling for 'ikhtartu' in cases of takhyir (choice to stay or divorce) is established by consensus of the Companions and is limited to that specific context.
4
Understand the rationale for the difference
'Ibanah' is a word used figuratively for divorce (كناية), so it can effect divorce. 'Ikhtiyar' is not a divorce word at all, so it cannot. The wife's use of 'abantu' includes an element of divorce, but adding a description of irrevocability is an attempt to change the nature; since the delegation is over explicit divorce (which is revocable), the description is void.
5
Note the internal Hanafi difference
Abu Hanifa reportedly held that 'abantu' does not cause divorce because the wife brought something other than what was delegated (i.e., separation instead of divorce). However, the apparent view is that 'ibanah' is a valid divorce word.
The mufta bihi is the apparent view.

Key Terms
كناية (kinayah): Implicit words that can be used for divorce but also have other meanings, requiring intention for divorce to occur.
تخيير (takhyir): Giving the wife the choice between staying married or being divorced.

Delegation of Divorce to Wife (Tamlik)
Ruling on husband delegating divorce to his wife

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between tamlik and tawkil in divorce delegation, and state the Hanafi ruling on when a wife can validly divorce herself after being told 'talqi nafsaki'.

Core Idea
Delegation of divorce (tamlik) is binding and confined to the council unless the husband adds 'mata shi'ti'.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling on a husband delegating the power of divorce to his wife. The text from Kanz al-Daqa'iq, expanded by Al-`Ayni and Al-Tahtawi, clarifies that such delegation is a form of ownership (tamlik) that is binding and tied to the council, with important exceptions. Understanding these distinctions is crucial for applying the rules of divorce correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The husband says 'talqi nafsaki' (divorce yourself). This is a delegation of divorce. The Hanafi ruling is that it is a binding act (tamlik) and not revocable by the husband.
Tamlik is distinct from tawkil (agency) in that it cannot be revoked.
2
Determine the condition of the council
As tamlik, the delegation requires a response in the same council (majlis). If the wife leaves or engages in a separate act, her option to divorce lapses.
The council is the place where the husband makes the statement.
3
Recognize exceptions based on additional words
If the husband adds 'mata shi'ti' (whenever you wish), the council restriction is removed. If he adds 'in shi'ti' (if you wish), it remains confined to the council.
The word 'mata' indicates generality of time.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يملك الرجوع [بعد قوله: طلقي نفسك حتى لا يصح نهيه؛ لأنه تصرف لازم. (ع)] أي لا يملك الزوج الرجوع عن التفويض بأنواعه الثلاث سواء كان بلفظ التخيير أو الأمر باليد أو طلقي نفسك؛ لأن فيه معنى التعليق وباعتبار التمليك تقيد بالمجلس وباعتبار التعليق لم يصح الرجوع عنه ولا عزلها ونهيها؛ لأن التعليق تصرف لازم فلا يصح الرجوع. (مستخلص، عيني) وتقيد بمجلسها الأنه تمليك فيختص بالمجلس حتى لو قامت عنه أو تحولت إلى مكان آخر أو أخذت في عمل آخر خرج الأمر من يدها. (ط)] أي لو قال لها: طلقي نفسك تقيد هذا التفويض بالمجلس؛ لأنه تمليك والتمليكات تقتضي جوابا في المجلس، ولها الخيار ما دامت في المجلس فإذا قامت أو أخذت بعمل آخر ثم طلقت نفسها لا يقع شيء؛ لأنه بطل خيارها بالقيام أو الأخذ بعمل آخر، وقوله: "إلا إذا زاد" متى شئت" استثناء من قوله : "تقيد بمجلسها" أي لو قال لها: طلقي نفسك متى شئت، لا يتقيد بالمجلس بل تطلق نفسها بعد القيام أيضاً؛ لأن كلمة "متى" عامة في الأوقات فصار كما إذا قال لها: طلقي نفسك في أي وقت شئت وكذا إذا شئت وإذا ما شئت. (عيني، مستخلص) إذا زاد: أي الزوج على قوله : طلقي نفسك. (ع) متى شئت فإنه يجوز أن تطلق نفسها في المجلس أو بعد القيام. (ط) بالمجلس: فله أن يطلقها في المجلس وبعده، وللزوج أن يرجع عنه؛ لأنه توكيل لا يشوبه تمليك ولا تعليق. (ط،ع) إلا إذا زاد إن شئت فإنه حينئذ يقتصر على المجلس؛ لأنه تمليك معنى وتعليق صورة ولا يصح رجوع الزوج (ع)]
And he does not have the right to revoke [after saying 'divorce yourself', so his prohibition is not valid because it is a binding act. (Al-`Ayni)] i.e., the husband does not have the right to revoke the delegation in its three types, whether by the word of choice, the command of the hand, or 'divorce yourself'; because it contains the meaning of suspension, and considering the ownership, it is tied to the council, and considering the suspension, revocation from it is not valid, nor her dismissal nor her prohibition; because suspension is a binding act, so revocation is not valid. (Mukhtasar, Al-`Ayni) And it is tied to her council because it is ownership, so it is specific to the council, so if she arises from it or moves to another place or begins another action, the matter leaves her hand. (Al-Tahtawi)] i.e., if he says to her 'divorce yourself', this delegation is tied to the council because it is ownership, and ownerships require a response in the council, and she has the choice as long as she is in the council. If she arises or begins another action then divorces herself, nothing occurs because her choice is invalidated by arising or beginning another action. And his statement 'except if he adds 'when you wish'' is an exception from his statement 'tied to her council' i.e., if he says to her 'divorce yourself when you wish', it is not tied to the council but rather she may divorce herself even after arising, because the word 'when' is general for times, so it is as if he said to her 'divorce yourself at any time you wish', and likewise 'if you wish' and 'when you wish'. (Al-`Ayni, Mukhtasar) If he adds: i.e., the husband to his statement 'divorce yourself' (Al-`Ayni) 'when you wish', then it is permissible for her to divorce herself in the council or after arising. (Al-Tahtawi) In the council: so he may divorce her in the council and after it, and the husband has the right to revoke it because it is agency that is not mixed with ownership nor suspension. (Al-Tahtawi, Al-`Ayni) Except if he adds 'if you wish', then it is restricted to the council because it is ownership in meaning and suspension in form, and the husband's revocation is not valid (Al-`Ayni)]
Source pages p. 431

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement about a husband delegating the power of divorce to his wife by saying 'talqi nafsaki' (divorce yourself). The text explains the Hanafi position that such a delegation is a form of tamlik (ownership) with an element of ta'liq (suspension). As tamlik, it is confined to the council (majlis) where the statement is made; if the wife leaves the place or engages in another act, her option lapses. However, the husband cannot revoke the delegation because of the suspensive element. An exception is made if the husband adds 'mata shi'ti' (whenever you wish), making it unrestricted by the council. If he adds 'in shi'ti' (if you wish), it remains confined to the council and also cannot be revoked. The text distinguishes between tamlik and tawkil (agency) in that the former is binding and tied to the council, while the latter is not. The commentary from Al-`Ayni and Al-Tahtawi elaborates on the details.

Key Terms
تمليك (tamlik): A delegation that vests ownership of the right to divorce in the wife, making it binding and confined to the council.
توكيل (tawkil): Agency where the husband authorizes someone else to divorce his wife, which is not confined to the council and can be revoked.
مجلس (majlis): The session or council where the delegation is made; tamlik requires a response in the same session.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a husband tells his wife 'talqi nafsaki' without any condition, when can she validly divorce herself?
A) Only in the same council
B) At any time until she remarries
C) Only after the husband confirms
D) At any time regardless of place

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, delegation of divorce (tamlik) is binding and confined to the council unless the husband specifies otherwise with unrestricted wording.

Delegating Divorce: When 'If You Wish' Changes Everything
Ruling on tawkil vs tamlik in divorce delegation with intra-Hanafi dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi distinction between tawkil and tamlik in divorce delegation, and apply the five rulings that differentiate them.

Core Idea
Adding 'if you wish' transforms a revocable agency into an irrevocable ownership-like delegation tied to the council.

A husband tells a friend 'Divorce my wife' — is the friend bound to act immediately? The Hanafi school distinguishes between a mere agency (tawkil) and a transfer of authority (tamlik) when the condition 'if you wish' is added. This lesson unpacks that distinction and five practical rulings that stem from it, including a disagreement with the Hanafi scholar Zufar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage describes two cases: (a) 'Talliq imra'ati' (divorce my wife) and (b) 'Talliq imra'ati in shi'ta' (divorce my wife if you wish). Recognize that the first is pure agency (tawkil), the second is disputed.
2
Understand the majority Hanafi position
Without the condition, it is tawkil: not tied to council, revocable. With the condition, it becomes tamlik: tied to council, irrevocable. The reason is that divorce admits suspension, so the condition creates a suspended ownership.
3
Examine Zufar's counterargument
Zufar argues that the condition does not change the nature; it remains agency because the agent still acts by his own choice, analogizing to a sale agent.
The Hanafi response is that sale does not admit suspension, so the analogy fails.
4
Learn the five differences between tamlik and tawkil
The passage enumerates five rulings where tamlik and tawkil differ: (1) tied to council, (2) husband's revocation allowed, (3) dismissal of wife's option valid, (4) effect of husband's insanity, (5) requirement of reason in the agent/wife.
Memorize these five points; they are a key Hanafi contribution.
5
Apply the mufta bihi position
The majority view (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) is the relied-upon position for fatwa. When in doubt, treat 'talliq in shi'ta' as tamlik.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هذا استثناء من قوله: "لم يتقيد بالمجلس" أي لو قال رجل لرجل: "طلق امرأتي" لا يتقيد بالمجلس؛ لأنه توكيل؛ إذ هو أمر بإيقاع الطلاق والأمر لا يقتضي وجوب الأشياء على الفور كما في أوامر الشرع التي مطلقة عن التوقيت إلا إذا قال: طلق امرأتي إن شئت فإنه يتقيد بالمجلس؛ لأنه لما علقه لمشيتها صار تمليكا منه فيقتضي جواباً في المجلس، وليس له أن يرجع عنه؛ لأنه تعليق صورة كما في "طلقي نفسك"، وقال زفر: هذا والأولى سواء؛ لأن التصريح بالمشيئة لا يقيد كعدمه؛ لأنه يتصرف عن مشيته، فصار كالوكيل بالبيع إذا قيل له "بعه إن شئت". ولنا: أنه تمليك؛ لأنه فوض الأمر إلى رأيه والمالك هو الذي يتصرف عن مشيته والطلاق يحتمل التعليق، بخلاف البيع؛ لأنه لا يحتمله. واعلم أن الفرق بين التمليك والتوكيل في خمسة أحكام فالتمليك يتقيد بالمجلس، ويصح الرجوع عنه، ولا يصح العزل، ولا يبطل بجنون الزوج ولا يشترط العقل فيه، وانعكست هذه الأحكام في التوكيل، فلا يتقيد بالمجلس ولا يصح الرجوع عنه والعزل، ويبطل بجنون المؤكل، ولا بد في صحة التوكيل من عقل الوكيل. (مستخلص، فتح)
This is an exception from his statement 'it is not tied to the council' i.e., if a man says to another man 'divorce my wife', it is not tied to the council because it is agency; since it is a command to effect divorce, and a command does not necessitate immediate performance like the commands of the law that are absolute regarding time, except if he says 'divorce my wife if you wish', then it is tied to the council because when he conditioned it on her will, it becomes tamlik from him, so it requires a response in the council, and he does not have the right to revoke it because it is suspension in form as in 'divorce yourself'. Zufar said: this and the first are the same, because the explicit mention of will does not tie just as its absence, because he acts according to his will, so it is like the agent in sale if he is told 'sell it if you wish'. And our proof: it is tamlik because he delegated the matter to his opinion, and the owner is the one who acts by his will, and divorce admits suspension, unlike sale because it does not admit it. And know that the difference between tamlik and tawkil is in five rulings: tamlik is tied to the council, and revocation from it is valid, and dismissal is not valid, and it is not invalidated by the husband's insanity, and reason is not required in it; and these rulings are reversed in tawkil: it is not tied to the council, revocation from it is not valid, dismissal is valid, it is invalidated by the principal's insanity, and the agent's reason is necessary for the validity of agency. (Mukhtasar, Fath)
Source pages p. 431

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute between the majority (Abu Hanifa and his students) and Zufar regarding a husband telling another man 'talliq imra'ati' (divorce my wife) with the condition 'in shi'ta' (if you wish). The Hanafi position holds that without the condition, it is pure agency (tawkil) and not confined to the council; the husband can revoke it. With the condition, it becomes tamlik (ownership) and is confined to the council, and the husband cannot revoke. Zufar argues that adding 'if you wish' does not change the ruling because the agent still acts by his own will, analogous to a sale agent. The Hanafi response is that divorce can be suspended, unlike sale, and thus the condition transforms the agency into tamlik. The passage concludes by listing five key differences between tamlik and tawkil: (1) tamlik is tied to the council, tawkil is not; (2) tamlik allows the husband to revoke, tawkil does not; (3) tamlik does not allow dismissal of the wife's option, tawkil does; (4) tamlik is not invalidated by husband's insanity, tawkil is; (5) tamlik does not require reason in the wife, tawkil requires reason in the agent.

Key Terms
توكيل (tawkil): Agency where the husband authorizes another to divorce his wife; not confined to council and revocable.
تمليك (tamlik): Ownership-like delegation that grants the wife (or agent) the right to divorce, tied to council and irrevocable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position, if a man tells another man 'talliq imra'ati in shi'ta', what is the ruling?
A) It is tawkil, not confined to council
B) It is tamlik, confined to council and irrevocable
C) It is tawkil, but confined to council
D) It is tamlik, but revocable

Key Takeaway
Adding 'if you wish' to a divorce delegation changes it from revocable agency (tawkil) to irrevocable ownership-like delegation (tamlik), tied to the council and with five distinct legal consequences.

Wife Exceeds or Undershoots Number in Delegation
Intra-Hanafi dispute on delegation of divorce numbers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a wife exceeds the delegated number of divorces and distinguish between Abu Hanifa's and the Sahibayn's positions.

Core Idea
When the wife exceeds the number, she becomes an initiator, not a responder, so nothing occurs according to Abu Hanifa.

In this lesson, we examine an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a husband's delegation of divorce to his wife. The key issue is whether the wife's action is considered a valid response to the delegation or an independent initiation. This hinges on the nature of the number — one versus three — and the source of authority: the husband acts from ownership, the wife from delegation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Understand the two cases: husband says 'divorce yourself three' and she divorces once, and the opposite where he says 'divorce yourself one' and she divorces three.
The first case is agreed upon, the second is disputed.
2
State Abu Hanifa's reasoning
For the second scenario, Abu Hanifa says nothing occurs because three is a composite number, one is simple; they are different in kind. The wife becomes a mubtadi'ah (initiator), not a mujibah (responder).
Her act does not match the delegation; she oversteps.
3
State the Sahibayn's reasoning
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad argue that one divorce occurs because she did what she was given (one) plus extra, analogous to a husband divorcing a thousand (which counts as three).
They view it as performing the delegated act with excess.
4
Note the exceptions and mufta bihi
The disagreement is limited to when she pronounces three in one sentence. If she pronounces them separately, or if the husband used 'amruki bi-yadiki' intending one, then one divorce occurs by consensus. The relied-upon view is Abu Hanifa's.
These exceptions show the boundaries of the dispute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقعت واحدة لا في عكسه، وطلقي نفسك ثلاثاً إن شئت فطلقت واحدةً، أي لا يقع شيء في وعكسه لا، ولو أمرها بالبائن أو الرّجعي فعكست وقع ما أمر به، أي في قوله وقعت واحدة: [ أي طلقة واحدة؛ لأن يملك من إيقاع الثلاث يملك إيقاع الواحدة ضرورة. (ع)] لأنها ملكت إيقاع الثلاث؛ لأن الزوج قال لها: "طلقي نفسك ثلاثاً" فتملك الواحدة بطريق الأولى، وقوله: "لا في عكسه" أي لو قال لها: "طلقي نفسك واحدة" فطلقت ثلاثاً لم يقع شيء عند أبي حنيفة، وقالا: تقع واحدة؛ لأنها أتت بما ملكته وزيادة فصار كما إذا طلقها الزوج ألفاً، ولأبي حنيفة أنها أتت بغير ما فوض إليها، فكانت مبتدأة لا مجيبة؛ لأن الزوج ملكها الواحدة، والثلاث غير الواحدة؛ لأن الثلاث اسم لعدد مركب مجتمع، والواحدة فرد لا تركيب فيه، فكانا غيرين، بخلاف الزوج؛ لأنه يتصرف بحكم الملك، والخلاف مقيد بما إذا وقعت الثلاثة بكلمة واحدة، أما إذا أوقعت واحدة وواحدة وواحدة وقعت واحدة اتفاقاً، وقيد بقوله: "طلقي"؛ لأنه لو قال: أمرك بيدك ينوي واحدة فطلقت ثلاثاً، وقعت واحدة اتفاقاً. (مستخلص، فتح)
It occurs one, not in its opposite. And if he says 'divorce yourself three if you wish' and she divorces once, i.e., nothing occurs, and its opposite nothing. And if he commands her with bain or raj'i and she does the opposite, what he commanded occurs. i.e., in his statement 'it occurs one': [i.e., one divorce; because the one who has the power to effect three has the power to effect one by necessity. (Al-`Ayni)] because she was given the power to effect three; since the husband said to her 'divorce yourself three', she possesses one a fortiori. And his statement 'not in its opposite' i.e., if he said to her 'divorce yourself one' and she divorced three, nothing occurs according to Abu Hanifa, and they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: one occurs because she did what she was given plus extra, so it is like if the husband divorced her a thousand. And for Abu Hanifa, she did other than what was delegated to her, so she is an initiator, not a responder; because the husband gave her ownership of one, and three is not one; because three is a name for a composite number, and one is a single with no composition, so they are different, unlike the husband (if he divorces) because he acts by virtue of ownership. And the disagreement is restricted to when the three occur with one word; but if she effects one and one and one, one occurs by agreement. And it is restricted by his word 'divorce' because if he said 'your affair is in your hand' intending one, and she divorced three, one occurs by agreement. (Mukhtasar, Fath)
Source pages p. 431

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) regarding a wife who exceeds or undershoots the number of divorces delegated to her. In the first scenario, the husband says 'talqi nafsaki thalathan' (divorce yourself three) and she divorces once: all agree it counts as one because she had the power to do three, so she can do one a fortiori. In the opposite scenario, he says 'talqi nafsaki wahidatan' (divorce yourself one) and she divorces three: Abu Hanifa rules nothing occurs because three is substantively different from one (a composite number vs. a single), so she overstepped the delegation. The Sahibayn argue that one occurs because she did what she was given (one) plus extra, analogous to a husband who divorces his wife a thousand times (which counts as three). The text notes that if she pronounces three divorces one at a time, all agree one occurs. Also, if he used the phrase 'amruki bi-yadiki' (your affair in your hand) intending one, and she divorces three, one occurs by agreement.

Key Terms
مبتدأة (mubtadi'ah): A wife who initiates divorce on her own rather than responding to the husband's delegation; her action is ineffective.
مجيبة (mujibah): A wife who responds properly to the delegation; her divorce is effective.

Key Takeaway
When a wife exceeds the delegated number of divorces, she is considered an initiator, and no divorce occurs according to the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Conditional Delegation with Number Contradiction
Ruling on conditional delegation when wife's action contradicts condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule on conditional divorce delegation when the wife pronounces a number different from the husband's condition, and explain the dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
When the condition specifies a number, the wife must will that exact number; willing a different number violates the condition and nullifies the delegation.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq examines a subtle scenario in conditional divorce delegation. The husband attaches 'in shi'ti' (if you wish) and states a specific number of divorces. The wife then pronounces a different number. Does the divorce occur? Abu Hanifa says no, while the Sahibayn argue for a partial effect in one case. We unpack the reasoning and final Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two cases
The text presents two symmetrical cases: (Case 1) husband says 'divorce yourself three if you wish', wife divorces once; (Case 2) husband says 'divorce yourself one if you wish', wife divorces three.
The condition in both uses 'in shi'ti', making the wife's will a prerequisite.
2
State Abu Hanifa's ruling
In both cases, Abu Hanifa rules that nothing occurs. The wife's will did not match the specified number, so she disobeyed the condition, rendering the delegation ineffective.
Condition must be fulfilled exactly; willing a different number is not compliance.
3
Analyze the Sahibayn's objection
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad) argue that in Case 2, willing three implies willing one, so one divorce should occur. They treat the larger will as inclusive of the smaller.
Their reasoning is based on the idea that three contains one, so the will for three necessarily includes will for one.
4
Understand the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is that the husband delegated the effecting of one divorce directly (qasdan), not as part of three. The wife must intend the exact number delegated; she cannot fulfill the condition by a larger intention.
The delegation is for the specific act of one divorce, not for any three that happen to include one.
5
Apply the principle to other variations
If the husband says 'divorce yourself two if you wish' and she divorces one, similar logic applies: nothing occurs, because willing two does not equate to willing one. The condition must be met exactly.
Consistency: the condition is a precise requirement, not a range.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

This passage deals with conditional delegation where the husband uses 'in shi'ti' (if you wish) along with a specified number.
