In the opposite case, he says 'talqi nafsaki wahidatan in shi'ti' and she divorces three: according to Abu Hanifa, nothing occurs because willing three is not the same as willing one; the delegation was for one, so she disobeyed. The Sahibayn argue that one occurs because willing three implies willing one. The Hanafi response is that the husband specifically delegated the one, not a part of three. The text notes that this is a further development of the previous dispute, now with the condition 'in shi'ti'.

Key Terms
مشيئة (mashi'a): Will or wish; when the husband attaches 'in shi'ti', the wife's divorce depends on her willing the specified number.

Key Takeaway
In conditional delegation ('in shi'ti'), the wife must will the exact number of divorces specified; willing a different number renders the delegation ineffective and no divorce occurs.

Wife Deviates from Specified Type of Divorce
Ruling when wife deviates from specified type of divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that when a wife is delegated divorce with a specific description (bain/raj'i) and she performs the opposite, the husband's intended divorce occurs, and distinguish this from cases where the deviation is in the substance (e.g., number).

Core Idea
A wife's deviation in the description of a delegated divorce does not change the substance; the divorce occurs as commanded.

When a husband delegates the power of divorce to his wife with a specific type—either irrevocable (bain) or revocable (raj'i)—and the wife pronounces the opposite type, what is the legal effect? This lesson unpacks the Hanafi position that the divorce takes effect according to the husband's command, not the wife's utterance, because the description is subordinate to the substance. We also explore an important objection comparing this to the case where a husband says 'one' and the wife says 'three,' revealing a critical distinction between description and substance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario and Ruling
State the scenario: husband commands a specific type of divorce (bain or raj'i); wife performs the opposite. The ruling: what the husband commanded occurs, and the wife's description is void.
Example: Husband says 'talqi nafsaki wahidatan ba'inatan', wife says 'anta taliqun wahidatan raj'iyatan' -> bain divorce occurs.
2
Understand the Reasoning: Asl vs Wasf
The husband delegated the substance (asl) of divorce with a description (wasf). The wife brought the same substance but changed the description. The origin is not nullified by the description, so the origin occurs with the husband's description.
This is based on the principle that the delegator's intention is given priority in the description.
3
Examine the Objection on Number (One vs Three)
The objection: if the deviation in description still yields the commanded divorce, then when a husband says 'one' and wife says 'three', why does nothing occur according to Abu Hanifa? Here the wife agreed in origin (saying 'I divorce myself') but opposed in number.
The objector sees inconsistency.
4
Grasp the Distinction: Number vs Description
The response: number (adad) is not a description of the divorce; it is part of the substance (the number of divorces being effected). Thus, changing the number is opposition in the origin of the effect, not just in description.
In Hanafi fiqh, 'one' and 'three' are different acts of divorce, not mere descriptions of the same act.
5
Apply to Similar Cases
The principle extends to any case where the wife is delegated with a condition (e.g., 'if you enter the house, you are divorced') and she acts contrary, but here the deviation is only in the description of the divorce itself.
Always distinguish between substance and description in delegated divorces.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو أمرها بالبائن أو الرّجعي فعكست وقع ما أمر به ويلغو ما وصفت لكونها مخالفة فيه. (ع)] لأن الزوج فوض إليها ذات الطلاق الوصف وأنها أتت بذات ما فوض إليها وخالفت في الوصف فصارت موافقة في أصل الطلاق ومخالفة في وصفه، ولا يجوز إبطال الأصل للوصف فيقع الأصل مع الوصف الذي ذكره الزوج اعتبارا لجانب التفويض، فإن قيل: إذا قال لها: طلقي نفسك واحدة فطلقت ثلاثاً لا يقع شيء عند أبي حنيفة مع أنها وافقت في الأصل وهي قولها: طلقت نفسي، وخالفت في الوصف وهو قولها: ثلاثاً، فكان أن ينبغي يقع واحدة عنده أيضاً، قلنا: الطلاق إذا قرن بالعدد العدد لا لفظ الطلاق على ما عرف وإذا كان كذلك كانت مخالفة في أصل الإيقاع. (مستخلص)
And if he commands her with bain or raj'i and she does the opposite, what he commanded occurs and her description is void because she opposed it. (Al-`Ayni)] Because the husband delegated to her the substance of divorce with a description, and she brought the same substance he delegated but opposed in the description, so she is agreeing in the origin of divorce and opposing in its description. It is not permissible to nullify the origin for the description, so the origin occurs with the description mentioned by the husband, considering the side of delegation. If it is said: when he says to her 'divorce yourself one' and she divorces three, nothing occurs according to Abu Hanifa, even though she agreed in origin (saying 'I divorce myself') and opposed in description (saying three), so it would be fitting that one also occur according to him. We say: when divorce is coupled with number, the number is not a description of the word of divorce as is known, and if so, her opposition is in the origin of the effect. (Mukhtasar)
Source pages p. 432

Commentary
This passage addresses a scenario where the husband commands a specific type of divorce, e.g., bain (irrevocable) or raj'i (revocable), and the wife performs the opposite type. The ruling is that what the husband commanded occurs, and the wife's description is void. For example, if he says 'talqi nafsaki wahidatan ba'inatan' and she says 'anta taliqun wahidatan raj'iyatan', the divorce takes effect as a bain divorce as commanded. The reasoning is that the husband delegated the substance (asl) of divorce with a specific description (wasf). She brought the substance but changed the description. The origin is not nullified by the description, so the origin occurs with the husband's intended description. The text then addresses a potential objection: why doesn't this principle apply to the earlier case where he says 'one' and she divorces three? The answer is that number (adad) is not a mere description; it changes the essence of the divorce itself, so opposing it is opposition in the origin.

Key Terms
بائن (ba'in): An irrevocable divorce where the husband cannot take back his wife without a new marriage.
رجعي (raj'i): A revocable divorce during the 'iddah period.
أصل (asl): The substance or essence of the divorce act, as opposed to its description.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Raj'i divorce
C) Both types
D) No divorce

Key Takeaway
In delegated divorce, the wife's deviation in description (bain/raj'i) does not affect the substance; the husband's commanded type takes effect, but deviation in number is a substantive change that nullifies the delegation.

Conditional Divorce: Wife's Wish Subject to a Condition
Ruling on wife's conditional response in delegated divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between a void and a valid conditional divorce when the wife attaches a condition to her wish, and apply the Hanafi rule that a non-existent condition voids the wife's statement.

Core Idea
If the wife's wish depends on a non-existent condition, her statement is void; if on a past condition, divorce takes effect.

This lesson examines a nuanced scenario in conditional divorce (ta'liq al-talaq). The husband says, 'You are divorced if you wish,' delegating the decision to the wife. The wife responds, 'I wish if you wish' or adds a further condition. The Hanafi school analyzes whether the wife's wish actually exists at the moment of her statement. The ruling hinges on whether the added condition refers to a non-existent matter (ma'dum) or a past event (madi). Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly applying the law of conditional divorce.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Husband's Statement
Recognize that the husband's phrase 'You are divorced if you wish' is a conditional divorce (ta'liq) where the wife's wish is the condition.
2
Examine the Wife's Response
Note whether she accepts unconditionally or adds a condition like 'if you wish' or 'if Zayd comes'.
3
Classify the Added Condition
Determine if the condition she attaches is for a non-existent future event (e.g., rain that has not occurred) or a past fact that is already fulfilled.
4
Apply the Hanafi Rule
For non-existent condition: her wish is deemed non-existent, so no divorce. For past condition: her wish is considered present, so divorce occurs.
5
Consider the Husband's Intention
Even if the husband says 'I wish' intending divorce, it does not create a divorce because the wife's statement is void; only an explicit new pronouncement would count.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أنت طالق إن شئت، فقالت: شِئتُ إن شئت، فقال: شئتُ ينوي الطلاق، أو قالت: مجيبة أنا أنت أي الزوج أنا حال كونه ناوياً الطلاق أي المرأة شئت إن كان كذا لمعدوم بطل، وإن كان لشيء مضى طلقت. لمعدوم: أي لشيء معدوم بأن قالت مثلاً: إذا جاء المطر وسال الميزاب. [رمز الحقائق: ٢٥١/١](ع) بطل : [ بطل كلامها في الوجهين ولم يقع شيء؛ لأنه علق طلاقها بالمشيئة المرسلة أنت بالمعلقة فلم يوجد الشرط فلا يقع شيء. (ع)] أي لو قال لها: أنت طالق. شئت فقالت المرأة شئت أنا إن شئت أنت، فقال أنا شئت، ناويا الطلاق لا يقع شيء وبطل كلامها؛ لأن الزوج علق طلاقها بمشيتها الموجودة في تلك و لم توجد تلك المشيئة؛ لأنها علقت وجود مشيئتها على مشيئة الزوج ووجود مشيئة الزوج غير معلوم لها والمعلق بالشرط معدوم قبل وجود الشرط فكانت مشيئتها معدومة قبل وجود مشيئة الزوج ولما نية الزوج فليس في كلام المرأة ما يدل على الطلاق فيصير الزوج شائيا طلاقها والنية لا تعمل في غير المذكور حتى لو قال: شئت طلاقك يقع إذا نوى، لأنه مبتدأ فكأنه قال أوجدت أو حصلت طلاقك. ولو قالت المرأة في جواب قول الزوج لها أنت طالق إن شئت": شئت أنا إن قدم زيد مثلا والحال أنه لم يقدم فلا يقع شيء أيضاً؛ لأن التعليق بمشيئته موجودة منها في تلك الحالة وهي علقت مشيئتها بأمر معدوم فلم توجد مشيئتها موجودة في تلك الحالة. لشيء مضى: [ أي ثبت وجوده صفة بشيء، وصورة المسألة قد ذكرت تحت شيء. (محشي)] أي لو قالت: شئت إن كان كذا لشيء ثبت وجوده بأن قالت شئت إن قدم زيد، وكان قد قدم. (ع) طلقت أي لو قال لها: أنت طالق إن شئت فقالت: شئت إن كان كذا لشيء مضى أي تقدم وجوده بأن قالت مثلا: شئت إن قدم زيد وقد قدم طلقت؛ لأن التعليق بشرط كائن تنجيز ، فإن قيل لما كان كذلك لوجب أن يكون التنجيز فيما إذا قال الزوج: هو يهودي إن كنت فعلت كذا أمس، وهو يعلم أنها قد فعله، ولو كان تنجيزاً لوجب تكفيره ولم تجب، قلنا: قد اختلف المشايخ في التكفير ولو سلم فنقول: هذه الألفاظ صارت كناية عن اليمين بالله تعالى فيما إذا علق بفعل المستقبل وكذا إذا كان ماضيا اعتبارا بالمستقبل تحميا عن تكفير المسلم. (عيني، مستخلص)
You are divorced if you wish, and she said: I wish if you wish, then he said: I wish, intending divorce, or she said: answering I (the wife) you (the husband) I (the husband) being intending divorce (the wife) I wish if it is such for non-existent it is void, and if for something past she is divorced. For non-existent: meaning for something non-existent, like she said: when rain comes and the spout flows. [ رمز الحقائق: 251/1] (ع) Void: [Her speech is void in both cases and nothing occurs because he suspended her divorce on an absolute wish suspended on a condition, so the condition did not occur, so nothing occurs. (ع)] That is if he said to her: You are divorced. I wish, and the woman said: I wish if you wish, then he said: I wish, intending divorce, nothing occurs and her speech is void because the husband suspended her divorce on her wish existing at that time and that wish did not exist because she conditioned the existence of her wish on the husband's wish and the existence of the husband's wish is unknown to her, and what is suspended on a condition is non-existent before the existence of the condition, so her wish was non-existent before the existence of the husband's wish. And because the husband intended [divorce], there is nothing in the woman's speech indicating divorce, so the husband becomes a wisher of her divorce, and intention does not operate on what is not mentioned, unless he said: I wish your divorce, it occurs if he intends, because it is a new beginning, as if he said: I caused or I effected your divorce. And if the woman said in response to the husband's saying to her 'You are divorced if you wish': I wish if Zayd comes, for example, and he has not come, then nothing occurs also, because the suspension is on her wish existing at that time, and she conditioned her wish on a non-existent matter, so her wish did not exist at that time. For something past: [Meaning its existence is proven as a description of something, and the form of the issue has been mentioned under 'something'. (محشي)] That is if she said: I wish if it is such for something whose existence is proven, like she said: I wish if Zayd came, and he had come. (ع) She is divorced: That is if he said to her: You are divorced if you wish, and she said: I wish if it is such for something past, i.e., its existence preceded, like she said: I wish if Zayd came, and he had come, she is divorced, because the suspension on a condition that exists is a direct pronouncement. If it is said: if it is like that, then it should be a direct pronouncement when the husband says: He is a Jew if you did such-and-such yesterday, and he knows she did it, and if it were a direct pronouncement it would necessitate his disbelief and it is not necessary; we say: the scholars have differed on disbelief, and even if we accept, we say: these phrases have become metonyms for swearing by Allah, when suspended on a future action, and similarly if past, by analogy with the future, to protect the Muslim from being declared an unbeliever. (عيني, مستخلص)
Source pages p. 433

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with explanation from the commentary on the matn. It addresses a conditional divorce scenario where the husband says 'You are divorced if you wish' (أنت طالق إن شئت). The wife responds 'I wish if you wish' (شئت إن شئت). The ruling distinguishes between two cases: (1) If the condition on which the wife's wish depends is something non-existent (معدوم) — for example, she says 'I wish if rain comes' and it does not rain — her speech is void (بطل) and no divorce occurs. The reasoning is that the husband suspended divorce on her actual wish (المشيئة الموجودة), but she conditioned her wish on an unknown or non-existent event, so the required wish never existed. Even if the husband says 'I wish' intending divorce, that does not create a divorce because the woman's speech does not indicate divorce, and intention cannot create an effect in a statement that does not mention divorce. (2) If the condition is something that has already occurred (شيء مضى) — for example, she says 'I wish if Zayd came' and he had indeed come — then the divorce takes effect because the condition is already fulfilled, and the statement becomes a direct pronouncement (تنجيز). A further analogy is discussed concerning oaths (يمين): if someone says 'He is a Jew if you did X yesterday' knowing it happened, that is not treated as direct pronouncement of disbelief to protect the Muslim. The passage is purely Hanafi; no ikhtilaf is mentioned here.

Key Terms
مشيئة (mashi'a): The wife's power or will to effect divorce; here used as a condition in delegation of divorce
بطل (batala): Void, legally ineffective; used to describe the wife's statement when condition is non-existent

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the husband says 'You are divorced if you wish' and the wife says 'I wish if rain comes' and it does not rain, what is the ruling?
A) The wife is divorced immediately
B) The wife's statement is void and no divorce occurs
C) The wife is divorced after she says 'I wish' regardless
D) The husband must repeat the statement

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a conditional divorce where the wife's wish depends on a non-existent condition is void; only if the condition is already fulfilled does the divorce take effect.
